Second Type of Tasdiq: Formal Kalam Proofs
Ghazali describes the second type of tasdiq based on formal kalam proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how formal kalam proofs produce firm belief based on accepted premises among scholars.

Core Idea
Formal kalam proofs generate belief through widely accepted premises in scholarly circles.

Ghazali continues his taxonomy of belief by describing the second type: belief that arises from formal theological arguments. These proofs rely on premises that are well-known and unquestioned among leading scholars, making them resistant to doubt. Let's examine how this type of belief works and why it is considered firm.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage for the second type, then its translation. Notice how Ghazali describes the source and strength of this belief.
The key phrase is 'formal kalam proofs built upon accepted matters'.
2
Identify the source of firmness
Why does this type produce a 'firm belief' that does not change even with the possibility of contrary evidence? The passage links it to the fame of the premises among major scholars and the aversion to doubting them.
3
Reflect on limitations
Consider that this type benefits 'in some matters' and 'in the case of people'. Not everyone is affected by formal proofs. Think about why this might be.
Ghazali implies that this type is effective but not universal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : أن يحصل بالأدلة الرسمية الكلامية المبنية على أمور مسلمة مصدق بها ، لاشتهارها بين أكابر العلماء ، وشفاعة إنكارها ، ونفرة النفوس عن إبداء المزيد فيها ، وهذا الجنس أيضا يفيد في بعض الأمور ، وفي حق الناس تصديقا جازما بحيث لا يتغير صاحبه بإمكان خلافه أصلا

الثالثة : أن يحصل التصديق بالأدلة الخطابية التي جرت العادة باستعمالها في المحاورة ، والمخاطبات الجارية في العادات وذلك يفيد في حق الأكثرين تصديقا ببادىء الرأى ، وسابق الفهم ، إذ لم يكن الباطل مشحونا بالتعصب ، وبرسوخ اعتقاد ، على خلاف مقتضى الدليل، ولم يكن المستمع مشغوفا بتكلف المماراة والتشكيك ، ومنهاجه بجدال المجادلين في العقائد ، وأكثر أدلة القرآن من هذا الجنس ، من الدليل الظاهر المفيد للتصديق ، والدليل المستوفي هو الذي يفيد التصديق بعد تمام الأسئلة وجوابها ، بحيث لا يبقى للسؤال مجال ، والتصديق يحصل قبل ذلك

الرابعة : التصديق بوجود السماع ممن حسن فيه الاعتقادة بسبب كثرة ثناء الخلق ، فإن من حَسُنَ اعتقاده في أبيه وأستاذه ، أو حسن اعتقاده في رجل من الأفاضل المشهورين ، قد يخبر عن شيء ، فيسبق إليه اعتقاد جازم ، وتصديق بما أخبر عنه ، بحيث لا يبقى مجال لغيره في قلبه ، ومستنده حسن اعتقاده فيه وكذلك اعتقاد الصبيان في آبائهم ومعلمهم فلا غرابة يسمعون الاعتقادات ويصدقونه ويستمرون عليه من غير حاجة إلى دليل ومناقشة

الخامسة : التصديق الذي يسبق إليه عند سماع الشيء مع قرائن الأحوال لا يفيد القطع عند المحقق ، ولكن يلقى في حق العوام اعتقادا جازما

السادسة : أن القول فيناسب طبعه أخلاقه فيبادر إلى التصديق بمجرد يسمع موافقته لطبعه الا من حسن اعتقاد في قائله ، ولا من قرينة تشهد له ، لكن لمناسبة ما في طبعه ، وهذه أضعف التصديقات ، وأدنى الدرجات ، لأن ما قبله استند إلى دليل ما وإن كان ضعيفا من قرينة ، أو حسن اعتقاد في المخبر ، أمارات يظنها العامي أدلة ، فتعمل في حقه عمل الأدلة
The second: That it occurs through formal kalam proofs built upon accepted and believed matters, due to their fame among the major scholars, and the difficulty of denying them, and the aversion of souls to expressing doubt in them. This type also benefits in some matters, and in the case of people it produces a firm belief such that its possessor does not change at all by the possibility of its opposite.

The third: That belief occurs through rhetorical proofs which are customarily used in conversation and customary dialogues. This benefits in the case of most people a belief at first sight and initial understanding, provided falsehood is not filled with fanaticism and deep-seated belief contrary to the requirement of the proof, and the listener is not fond of the effort of disputation and skepticism. Most of the proofs of the Quran are of this type: the apparent proof that yields belief, while the comprehensive proof is that which yields belief after the completion of questions and their answers such that there is no room for questioning, and belief occurs before that.

The fourth: Belief by hearing from one whose trustworthiness is established due to the abundance of people's praise. For one whose trust in his father and teacher is good, or whose trust in a famous virtuous man is good, may inform of something, and a firm belief rushes to him, and he believes what he was told, such that no room remains in his heart for other than it. Its basis is his good trust in him. Similarly is the belief of children in their fathers and teachers; without surprise they hear beliefs and believe them and continue upon them without need for proof or discussion.

The fifth: The belief that rushes to one upon hearing something along with circumstantial indications; it does not yield certainty for the investigator, but it casts in the case of common people a firm belief.

The sixth: That the statement suits his nature and character, so he hastens to believe just by hearing it agreeing with his nature, without reliance on good trust in its speaker, nor a circumstantial indication that witnesses for it, but due to suitability in his nature. This is the weakest of beliefs and the lowest of degrees, because what preceded it relied on some proof, though weak, from circumstantial indication or good trust in the informant - signs that the common man considers proofs, so they act in his case as proofs.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of five types of belief (tasdiq) beyond the first type which was mentioned earlier (not in this excerpt). The author classifies the ways in which ordinary people acquire belief in religious matters. He lists them from second to sixth: 2) formal kalam proofs, 3) rhetorical proofs like Quranic argumentation, 4) reliance on a trustworthy informant, 5) circumstantial indications, 6) mere compatibility with one's nature. He notes that most Quranic proofs are of the third type. The sixth is the weakest, based solely on personal inclination, while the earlier types involve some form of evidence or authority.

Key Terms
التصديق
الأدلة الرسمية الكلامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what makes the second type of tasdiq 'firm'?
A) It is based on logical necessity
B) It relies on premises famous among major scholars
C) It comes from direct sensory experience
D) It is confirmed by multiple witnesses

Key Takeaway
Formal kalam proofs produce firm belief by relying on widely accepted premises among scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you satisfied with a faith that rests on the fame of scholars rather than on direct certainty? What would happen if you discovered that a respected scholar you trusted actually doubted a premise you've taken for granted?
?
Have you ever silenced your own doubts about a widely held belief because it was 'difficult to deny' or because you felt your soul recoiled from questioning it? Is that reluctance a sign of humility or fear?
?
Ghazali says this type of belief is beneficial only in some matters and for some people. Where in your own life have you placed your trust in scholarly consensus without verifying it yourself? Will you continue to do so, or will you seek a deeper conviction?

Third Type of Tasdiq: Rhetorical Proofs
Ghazali explains the third type of tasdiq based on rhetorical proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how rhetorical proofs, like those in the Quran, create belief at first sight in most people.

Core Idea
Rhetorical proofs yield immediate belief for most people unless prejudice or skepticism intervenes.

The third type of belief comes from rhetorical proofs used in everyday conversation. Ghazali notes that most proofs in the Quran are of this kind. They work for the majority of people by producing an immediate conviction, though they can be undermined by fanaticism or a habit of disputation. Let's see how this type functions and why it is effective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the third type
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the terms 'rhetorical proofs' and 'apparent proof'.
Notice that Ghazali contrasts 'apparent proof' with 'comprehensive proof'.
2
Understand the effect of fanaticism
Why does belief from rhetorical proofs not occur in some people? The passage mentions falsehood filled with fanaticism and deep-seated contrary belief.
Also, the listener being fond of disputation can block belief.
3
Distinguish two sub-types
Identify the 'apparent proof' and the 'comprehensive proof' in the passage. Note that belief occurs before the comprehensive proof is completed.

Fourth Type of Tasdiq: Trust in a Reliable Informant
Ghazali describes the fourth type of tasdiq based on trust in a reliable informant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how belief can arise from relying on a trustworthy person, such as a father, teacher, or reputable figure.

Core Idea
Belief from trust in a reliable informant is firm and requires no external proof.

The fourth type of belief is based on trust in an informant whose credibility is established through widespread praise. This is how children believe their parents and teachers. The believer accepts the information without need for proof or discussion, solely because of the informant's perceived trustworthiness. Let's see how this type operates and why it is so powerful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the fourth type
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the examples given: father, teacher, famous virtuous man.
2
Identify the basis of belief
What is the 'basis' (mustanad) of this belief? The passage says it is 'good trust' (ḥusn al-iʿtiqād) in the informant.
This trust comes from 'the abundance of people's praise.'
3
Compare with children's belief
Ghazali compares this to how children believe their fathers and teachers without proof. What does this tell us about the naturalness of this type of belief?

The author classifies the ways in which ordinary people acquire belief in religious matters. He lists them from second to sixth: 2) formal kalam proofs, 3) rhetorical proofs like Quranic argumentation, 4) reliance on a trustworthy informant, 5) circumstantial indications, 6) mere compatibility with one's nature. He notes that most Quranic proofs are of the third type. The sixth is the weakest, based solely on personal inclination, while the earlier types involve some form of evidence or authority.

Key Terms

حسن الاعتقاد
المخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that belief from authority is weak or irrational.
Correction: Ghazali shows it can produce firm and enduring belief, especially in children and laypeople.

A) Logical demonstration
B) Good trust in the informant
C) Circumstantial evidence
D) Personal experience

Key Takeaway
Belief based on trust in a reliable informant is firm and needs no external proof.

Fifth Type of Tasdiq: Circumstantial Indications
Ghazali describes the fifth type of tasdiq based on circumstantial indications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how circumstantial indications (qarāʾin al-aḥwāl) can produce firm belief in common people, though not certainty for the investigator.

Core Idea
Circumstantial indications create firm belief in laypeople but not certainty for skilled investigators.

The fifth type of belief arises from circumstantial clues that accompany a statement. While these do not produce logical certainty for a critical investigator, they often create a firm conviction in the minds of common people. Ghazali ranks this below the previous types in epistemic strength. Let's explore this type and its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the fifth type passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the key term 'circumstantial indications' (qarāʾin al-aḥwāl).
2
Distinguish between levels
The passage says this type 'does not yield certainty for the investigator' but casts 'a firm belief' in common people. Why the difference?
Investigators demand rigorous proof, while common people are moved by circumstantial clues.
3
Compare with previous types
How does this type differ from the fourth type (trust in informant)? Here, no prior trust in the speaker is mentioned; it's about the circumstances of the utterance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : أن يحصل بالأدلة الرسمية الكلامية المبنية على أمور مسلمة مصدق بها ، لاشتهارها بين أكابر العلماء ، وشفاعة إنكارها ، ونفرة النفوس عن إبداء المزيد فيها ، وهذا الجنس أيضا يفيد في بعض الأمور ، وفي حق الناس تصديقا جازما بحيث لا يتغير صاحبه بإمكان خلافه أصلا

الثالثة : أن يحصل التصديق بالأدلة الخطابية التي جرت العادة باستعمالها في المحاورة ، والمخاطبات الجارية في العادات وذلك يفيد في حق الأكثرين تصديقا ببادىء الرأى ، وسابق الفهم ، إذ لم يكن الباطل مشحونا بالتعصب ، وبرسوخ اعتقاد ، على خلاف مقتضى الدليل، ولم يكن المستمع مشغوفا بتكلف المماراة والتشكيك ، ومنهاجه بجدال المجادلين في العقائد ، وأكثر أدلة القرآن من هذا الجنس ، من الدليل الظاهر المفيد للتصديق ، والدليل المستوفي هو الذي يفيد التصديق بعد تمام الأسئلة وجوابها ، بحيث لا يبقى للسؤال مجال ، والتصديق يحصل قبل ذلك

الرابعة : التصديق بوجود السماع ممن حسن فيه الاعتقادة بسبب كثرة ثناء الخلق ، فإن من حَسُنَ اعتقاده في أبيه وأستاذه ، أو حسن اعتقاده في رجل من الأفاضل المشهورين ، قد يخبر عن شيء ، فيسبق إليه اعتقاد جازم ، وتصديق بما أخبر عنه ، بحيث لا يبقى مجال لغيره في قلبه ، ومستنده حسن اعتقاده فيه وكذلك اعتقاد الصبيان في آبائهم ومعلمهم فلا غرابة يسمعون الاعتقادات ويصدقونه ويستمرون عليه من غير حاجة إلى دليل ومناقشة

الخامسة : التصديق الذي يسبق إليه عند سماع الشيء مع قرائن الأحوال لا يفيد القطع عند المحقق ، ولكن يلقى في حق العوام اعتقادا جازما

السادسة : أن القول فيناسب طبعه أخلاقه فيبادر إلى التصديق بمجرد يسمع موافقته لطبعه الا من حسن اعتقاد في قائله ، ولا من قرينة تشهد له ، لكن لمناسبة ما في طبعه ، وهذه أضعف التصديقات ، وأدنى الدرجات ، لأن ما قبله استند إلى دليل ما وإن كان ضعيفا من قرينة ، أو حسن اعتقاد في المخبر ، أمارات يظنها العامي أدلة ، فتعمل في حقه عمل الأدلة
The second: That it occurs through formal kalam proofs built upon accepted and believed matters, due to their fame among the major scholars, and the difficulty of denying them, and the aversion of souls to expressing doubt in them. This type also benefits in some matters, and in the case of people it produces a firm belief such that its possessor does not change at all by the possibility of its opposite.

The third: That belief occurs through rhetorical proofs which are customarily used in conversation and customary dialogues. This benefits in the case of most people a belief at first sight and initial understanding, provided falsehood is not filled with fanaticism and deep-seated belief contrary to the requirement of the proof, and the listener is not fond of the effort of disputation and skepticism. Most of the proofs of the Quran are of this type: the apparent proof that yields belief, while the comprehensive proof is that which yields belief after the completion of questions and their answers such that there is no room for questioning, and belief occurs before that.

The fourth: Belief by hearing from one whose trustworthiness is established due to the abundance of people's praise. For one whose trust in his father and teacher is good, or whose trust in a famous virtuous man is good, may inform of something, and a firm belief rushes to him, and he believes what he was told, such that no room remains in his heart for other than it. Its basis is his good trust in him. Similarly is the belief of children in their fathers and teachers; without surprise they hear beliefs and believe them and continue upon them without need for proof or discussion.

The fifth: The belief that rushes to one upon hearing something along with circumstantial indications; it does not yield certainty for the investigator, but it casts in the case of common people a firm belief.

The sixth: That the statement suits his nature and character, so he hastens to believe just by hearing it agreeing with his nature, without reliance on good trust in its speaker, nor a circumstantial indication that witnesses for it, but due to suitability in his nature. This is the weakest of beliefs and the lowest of degrees, because what preceded it relied on some proof, though weak, from circumstantial indication or good trust in the informant - signs that the common man considers proofs, so they act in his case as proofs.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of five types of belief (tasdiq) beyond the first type which was mentioned earlier (not in this excerpt). The author classifies the ways in which ordinary people acquire belief in religious matters. He lists them from second to sixth: 2) formal kalam proofs, 3) rhetorical proofs like Quranic argumentation, 4) reliance on a trustworthy informant, 5) circumstantial indications, 6) mere compatibility with one's nature. He notes that most Quranic proofs are of the third type. The sixth is the weakest, based solely on personal inclination, while the earlier types involve some form of evidence or authority.

Key Terms
التصديق
قرائن الأحوال

A) The investigator (muḥaqqiq)

Circumstantial indications produce firm belief in common people but not certainty for investigators.

Sixth Type of Tasdiq: Compatibility with Nature
Ghazali describes the sixth type of tasdiq based on compatibility with nature and declares it the weakest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief based solely on personal inclination is the weakest type of tasdiq, lacking any external evidence.

Core Idea
Belief based on compatibility with nature is the weakest, resting only on personal inclination.

The sixth and final type of belief is when a statement simply matches one's nature and character, leading to immediate acceptance. Unlike the previous types, there is no reliance on a trustworthy person or any circumstantial clue—just personal affinity. Ghazali declares this the weakest of all beliefs. Let's see why it is considered the lowest degree.

Guided Path
1
Read the sixth type passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that this type lacks any external support.
2
Identify what is missing
The passage says there is no good trust in the speaker, no circumstantial indication. Only 'suitability in his nature.'
3
Understand its weakness
Why is this the weakest? Because previous types had at least some proof or indication. Here, there is none.
Ghazali calls it 'the weakest of beliefs and the lowest of degrees.'

The Highest Degree of Belief for Common People
Ghazali concludes that for common people, the best evidence is the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali limits common people to Quranic proofs and why this is the highest degree for them.

Core Idea
For common people, the Quran's proofs are the safest and highest form of belief.

Ghazali has explained the ranks of belief. Now he draws a practical conclusion: the common person should not be taken beyond the Quran's clear, heart-soothing proofs. This lesson explores that guidance and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key phrases about 'turning the heart' and 'capacity'.
The opening phrase may be unclear due to OCR; focus on the overall meaning.
2
Identify the highest level for common people
Ghazali states that the highest degree for common people is 'the proofs of the Noble Quran and what runs in its course.' Find this in the text.
Contrast this with what lies beyond.
3
Ask why not to go beyond
Ghazali says going beyond is 'not within his capacity.' Reflect on why speculative theology might be too difficult or harmful for the common person.
Consider the Quran's role in providing tranquility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك فأي نوع من فهي القطعية ، واذا علم مراتب التصديق ، وعلم أن مستند إيمان العوام هذه الأسباب ، فأعلى الدرجات في حقه أدلة القرآن الكريم ، وما يجري مجراه مما يحول القلب إلى التصديق ، فلا ينبغى أن يجاوز بالعامي إلى ما وراء أدلة القرآن ، وما في معناه من الجليات المقنعة المسكنة للقلوب ، المستجرة لها إلى الطمأنينة والتصديق ، فما وراء ذلك ليس على قدر طاقته
That, so which type from these is certain? And when the ranks of belief are known, and it is known that the basis of the common people's faith is these causes, then the highest degree in their case is the proofs of the Noble Quran and what runs in its course that turns the heart to belief. So one should not go beyond with the common person beyond the proofs of the Quran and what is in their meaning of clear, convincing, heart-soothing things that draw them to tranquility and belief. For what is beyond that is not within his capacity.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage draws the practical conclusion from the earlier enumeration. Ghazali states that once we understand the different levels of belief and that the common people's faith rests on these various causes, the highest and safest level for them is the Quranic proofs and similar clear arguments. They should not be taken into speculative theology (kalam) beyond that, as it is beyond their capacity. The phrase 'that which turns the heart to belief' emphasizes the Quran's persuasive power over the average person.

Key Terms
مراتب التصديق
العوام
أدلة القرآن
الجليات المقنعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Common people should study rational theology (kalam) to strengthen their faith.
Correction: Ghazali teaches that the Quran's proofs are sufficient and safer; speculative theology is beyond their capacity and may cause confusion.

Key Takeaway
Common people should attain the highest degree of belief through the Quran's clear and heart-soothing proofs, not through speculative theology.

Tawheed as Negation and Affirmation
Ghazali explains the meaning of a hadith and verse, showing that tawheed requires both negation and affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the testimony of tawheed (La ilaha illallah) necessarily includes both negation and affirmation, and how this is rooted in the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Tawheed is neither pure negation nor pure affirmation—it is both together.

This lesson explores a key concept in Islamic theology: the shahada ‘La ilaha illallah’ is not just a phrase but a comprehensive declaration that simultaneously negates false gods and affirms the true God. Imam al-Ghazali explains this using a prophetic hadith and a Quranic verse, showing that worship is only valid when it is free from shirk and directed to Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Ghazali uses both hadith and Quran as evidence.
2
Identify negation and affirmation
Find where Ghazali explicitly mentions 'negation' (نفي) and 'affirmation' (إثبات). Note how he connects them to the shahada and to Surah al-Kafirun.
3
Understand why both are necessary
Ghazali says that pure negation is not tawheed, nor is affirmation without negation. Ask yourself: why would saying only 'There is no god' or only 'Allah is God' be insufficient? The commentary will help.
This connects to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « أن يعبدوه ولا يشركوا به شيئا » الزام للعباد بأن يوحدوه بالعبادة وحده ولا يشركوا به شيئا. وفائدة هذه الجملة : بيان بأن التجرد من الشرك لابد منه في العبادة ، وإلا فلا يكون العبد آتيا بعبادة الله تعالى ، بل مشرك في عبادته. وهذا هو معنى قول من قال : إن العبادة هي التوحيد ، لأن الخصومة فيه ، وفيه معرفة حق الله على العباد ، وهو عبادته وحده لا شريك له سبحانه. قال تعالى : ﴿ قُلْ إِنَّمَا أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أَعْبُدَ اللهَ وَلَا أُشْرِكَ بِهِ ، إِلَيْهِ ادْعُوا وَإِلَيْهِ مَآب ﴾ (1). وهذه الآية الكريمة هي معنى : لا إله إلا الله ، لأنها تضمنت النفي والاثبات ، التي تضمنته لا إله إلا الله، كما دلت على أنه لا بد في الاسلام من النفي والاثبات ، فيثبت العبادة الله وحده ، وينفي عبادة ما سواه وهو التوحيد الذي تضمنته سورة : قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الْكَافِرُونَ (2). فينفي عبادة ما سوى الله ، ويثبت عبادته سبحانه ، وهذا هو حقيقة التوحيد ، والنفي المحض ليس بتوحيد، وكذلك الاثبات بدون النفي ، فلا يكون التوحيد إلا متضمنا للنفي والاثبات ، وهذا حقيقة لا إله إلا الله.
And in His saying, peace be upon him, 'that they worship Him and do not associate anything with Him' is an obligation upon the slaves to single Him out in worship alone and not associate anything with Him. The benefit of this sentence is the statement that purification from shirk is necessary in worship, otherwise the slave would not be performing the worship of Allah Almighty, but rather would be a mushrik in his worship. This is the meaning of the statement of those who said that worship is tawheed, because the dispute is about it, and in it is the knowledge of Allah's right over the slaves, which is to worship Him alone with no partner, glory be to Him. Allah Almighty said: {Say: I am only commanded to worship Allah and not to associate anything with Him; to Him I call and to Him is my return} (1). And this noble verse is the meaning of 'La ilaha illallah', because it includes negation and affirmation, which are included in 'La ilaha illallah', as it indicates that in Islam there must be negation and affirmation, so he affirms worship of Allah alone, and negates worship of other than Him, and this is the tawheed which is contained in Surah 'Say: O disbelievers' (2). So he negates worship of other than Allah, and affirms worship of Him, glory be to Him, and this is the reality of tawheed. Pure negation is not tawheed, nor is affirmation without negation. So tawheed is only real when it includes negation and affirmation, and this is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah'.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage defines the meaning of 'La ilaha illallah' as requiring both negation and affirmation. The author begins by quoting the hadith 'that they worship Him and do not associate anything with Him' as an obligation upon slaves to single out Allah in worship. He then states the benefit: purification from shirk is necessary in worship; otherwise it is not true worship. He connects this to the statement that worship is tawheed. Then he cites Quran 13:36, which contains both negation ('I am not to associate') and affirmation ('I am commanded to worship Allah'). He says this verse is the meaning of 'La ilaha illallah' because it includes both elements. The author explains that Islam requires both negation (of other gods) and affirmation (of Allah alone). He refers to Surah al-Kafirun as another example. He concludes that pure negation is not tawheed, nor is affirmation without negation; tawheed must include both, and that is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah'.

Key Terms
لا إله إلا الله
توحيد
نفي
إثبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that saying 'La ilaha illallah' is enough without understanding its meaning of negation and affirmation.
Correction: The passage shows that the phrase inherently includes both negation and affirmation, and tawheed is not valid without understanding and intending both.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah'?
A) Only negation of other gods
B) Only affirmation of Allah
C) Both negation and affirmation
D) Either negation or affirmation

Key Takeaway
Tawheed is the combination of negating all false objects of worship and affirming exclusive worship for Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says worship is tawheed. Is your worship (prayer, charity, etc.) directed solely to Allah, or are you seeking the approval of others? How can you purify your intention this week?

The Right of Slaves upon Allah Explained
Ghazali explains the hadith's condition and Ibn Kathir's interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct interpretation of the hadith 'the right of slaves upon Allah' and why it implies not just avoidance of shirk but also belief in prophethood and obedience.

Core Idea
The hadith's promise is for complete faith, not mere lack of shirk.

The hadith 'The right of the slaves upon Allah is that He will not punish whoever does not associate anything with Him' might seem to guarantee salvation just by avoiding shirk. However, Imam al-Ghazali and Ibn Kathir clarify that this promise is conditional upon true worship and belief in all that must be believed, including prophethood. Let's explore how they arrive at this understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its English translation. Pay attention to how Ghazali connects the hadith to worship (commands and prohibitions) and then to Ibn Kathir's commentary.
Notice that the passage moves from a general statement to a deeper theological explanation.
2
Understand Ghazali's direct explanation
Ghazali states that the hadith refers to those who worship Allah and do not associate partners. He emphasizes that worship includes performing commands and avoiding prohibitions, because mere absence of shirk does not negate punishment (as evidenced by threats against sinners).
This shows that the hadith is not a blanket guarantee.
3
Analyze Ibn Kathir's logical inference
Ibn Kathir explains why the hadith mentions only negation of shirk: it implies tawheed by necessity and also implies belief in prophethood by entailment. Denying the messenger is equivalent to denying Allah, which is shirk.
Thus the hadith's condition implicitly includes all articles of faith.
4
Consider the wudu analogy
Ibn Kathir gives an analogy: 'Whoever performs wudu, his prayer is valid' means along with other conditions. Similarly, 'whoever does not associate' means along with all other required beliefs and actions.
This clarifies that the hadith is not a standalone promise.
5
Apply the correct understanding
Reflect on the common misunderstanding that merely avoiding shirk guarantees salvation. The passage teaches that genuine faith requires belief in prophethood, obedience to commands, and avoidance of prohibitions.
This lesson safeguards against a shallow interpretation of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي قوله : وحق العباد على الله أن لا يعذب من لا يشرك به شيئا، بيان أن الله لا يعذب من يعبده ، ولا يشرك به شيئا ، وأن العبادة هي الإتيان بالاوامر والانتهاء عن النواهي ، لأن مجرد عدم الاشراك لا يقتضي نفي العذاب ، وقد علم ذلك من القرآن الكريم ، والاحاديث الشريفة ، الواردة في تهديد الظالمين والعصاة . يقول الامام الحافظ ابن كثير رحمه الله تعالى : اقتصر على نفي الاشراك لأنه يستدعي التوحيد بالاقتضاء ، ويستدعي إثبات الرسالة باللزوم ، إذ من كذب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فقد كذب الله تعالى ، ومن كذب الله تعالى فهو مشرك ، وهو مثل قول القائل : من توضأ صحت صلاته ، أى مع سائر الشروط ، فالمراد من مات حال كونه مؤمنا بجميع ما يجب الإيمان به.
And in His saying: 'And the right of the slaves upon Allah is that He will not punish whoever does not associate anything with Him' is a statement that Allah will not punish whoever worships Him and does not associate anything with Him, and that worship is the performance of commands and the abstention from prohibitions, because mere lack of shirk does not negate punishment, and that is known from the Noble Qur'an and the noble hadiths that threaten oppressors and sinners. Imam al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'He confined to the negation of shirk because it implies tawheed by necessity, and implies the affirmation of prophethood by entailment, since whoever denies the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, has denied Allah Almighty, and whoever denies Allah Almighty is a mushrik. It is like the saying of someone: 'Whoever performs wudu, his prayer is valid', i.e., along with the rest of conditions. So the intended meaning is whoever dies while being a believer in all that must be believed in.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage explains the hadith about the right of slaves upon Allah, that He will not punish those who do not associate partners. The author first clarifies that this refers to those who worship Him and do not associate, and that worship includes performing commands and avoiding prohibitions. He notes that mere absence of shirk does not negate punishment, as the Quran and hadith threaten oppressors and sinners. Then he quotes Imam Ibn Kathir, who says that the hadith confined to negation of shirk because it implies tawheed by necessity and also implies belief in prophethood by entailment, since denying the messenger is like denying Allah, which is shirk. Ibn Kathir gives an analogy: 'whoever performs wudu, his prayer is valid' means along with the rest of conditions. So the intended meaning is 'whoever dies while being a believer in all that must be believed in.' Thus the hadith does not guarantee salvation merely by lack of shirk, but by complete faith and obedience.

Key Terms
حق العباد
عذاب
شرك
رسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply avoiding shirk guarantees salvation, without needing to believe in prophethood or obey Allah's commands.
Correction: The hadith's phrase 'does not associate' is shorthand for complete faith, which includes belief in prophethood and obedience, as clarified by Ibn Kathir's analogy of wudu conditions.

Checkpoint
Why did the hadith confine to negation of shirk according to Ibn Kathir?
A) Because it is easier
B) Because it implies tawheed and prophethood
C) Because worship is not required
D) Because shirk is the only sin

Key Takeaway
The hadith's promise of no punishment for those who do not associate partners is conditional upon complete faith, including belief in prophethood and obedience to Allah's commands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on the mere fact that you believe in Allah and have never committed shirk, while neglecting sins that you have normalized in your life? What must you change today to move from minimal faith to complete obedience as defined in this lesson?
?
The hadith promises salvation only for those who 'worship Him and do not associate anything with Him.' Look at your daily routine: where are you worshipping Allah through obedience, and where are you following your desires against His commands? Will you start a specific action to align your actions with what you just read?
?
If your salvation depended on the sincerity of your belief in prophethood as Ibn Kathir explained, would you be confident? Examine your relationship with the Prophet's sunnah: are you selective in following it? What is one way you can increase your commitment to his teachings starting this week?

The Living Reality of Tawheed
Ghazali defines the reality of tawheed as soul's total devotion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the reality of tawheed is a complete orientation of the soul towards Allah, encompassing knowledge, action, and heartfelt devotion.

Core Idea
Tawheed is not a word but total devotion of the soul to Allah.

Imam al-Ghazali now takes us beyond the formula of 'La ilaha illallah' into its living reality. He insists that true tawheed is not just a verbal confession but a state where the entire soul is drawn to Allah, leaving no room for anything else. This passage challenges us to examine whether our faith is merely outward or deeply rooted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the words sink in before analysis.
Notice the density of meaning in a few lines.
2
Identify the core definition
Find where Ghazali says 'the reality of tawheed is...' and note the two components: knowledge/insight and action.
3
Examine the list of states
He lists ten states that describe the soul's attraction to Allah. Write them down and reflect on each.
These are love, fear, turning, trust, supplication, sincerity, veneration, awe, magnification, worship.
4
Connect to the shahada
Ghazali concludes that this is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah'. Ask yourself how this changes your understanding of the testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحقيق التوحيد : هو معرفته والاطلاع على حقيقته ، والقيام بها علما وعملا ، وحقيقة ذلك هو انجذاب الروح إلى الله تعالى ، محبة ، وخوفا ، وإنابة ، وتوكلا ، ودعاء ، وإخلاصا ، واجلالا ، وهيبة ، وتعظيما وعبادة . وبالجملة : فلا يكون في قلبه شيء لغير الله سبحانه ، ولا إرادة لما حرم الله ، ولا كراهة لما أمر الله ، وذلك هو حقيقة : «لا إله إلا الله » فإن الاله هو المألوه المعبود وذلك هو حقيقة الشهادتين ، فمن قام بهما على هذا الوجه فهو من الذين يدخلون الجنة.
And the reality of tawheed is: knowledge of it and insight into its truth, and acting upon it in knowledge and practice. Its true reality is the attraction of the soul to Allah Almighty, in love, fear, turning in repentance, trust, supplication, sincerity, veneration, awe, magnification, and worship. In summary: there is nothing in his heart for other than Allah Almighty, no desire for what Allah has forbidden, no dislike of what Allah has commanded. That is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah', for al-ilah is the one worshipped. That is the reality of the two testimonies. Whoever fulfills them in this manner is among those who enter paradise.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of tawheed. The author states that the reality of tawheed is knowledge of it, insight into its truth, and acting upon it in knowledge and practice. Its true reality is the attraction of the soul to Allah Almighty through various states: love, fear, turning in repentance, trust, supplication, sincerity, veneration, awe, magnification, and worship. In summary, there is nothing in the heart for other than Allah, no desire for what He has forbidden, and no dislike of what He has commanded. That is the reality of 'La ilaha illallah', for 'al-ilah' means the one who is worshipped. This is the reality of the two testimonies (shahadatayn). Whoever fulfills them in this manner is among those who enter paradise.

Misconception: Tawheed is merely saying the words 'La ilaha illallah' without any inner transformation or practical devotion.
Correction: Ghazali shows that true tawheed is knowledge, action, and the soul's total attraction to Allah, leaving no room for anything else.

Checkpoint

A) Just saying the words
B) Knowledge and action, and attraction of the soul to Allah in devotion
C) Only worship acts
D) Belief in Allah without works

Key Takeaway
True tawheed is not just saying the words but a complete inner and outer devotion to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If Allah were to examine your heart tonight, would He find anything occupying it besides Him? What would that thing be, and when will you begin to remove it?

The Hadith of Rights: Tawhid Requires Action
Imam Ghazali explains the hadith of rights and Ibn Kathir’s commentary on its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true tawhid demands not only avoiding shirk but actively performing commands and refraining from prohibitions, and that negation of shirk implies belief in prophethood.

Core Idea
Tawhid is more than 'just don't associate'—it demands active worship and implies faith in the Prophet.

This lesson unpacks a famous hadith about the rights of Allah and His servants. Imam Ghazali explains that mere non-association does not guarantee salvation; worship requires action. He then quotes Ibn Kathir’s insightful commentary showing how the hadith implicitly affirms tawhid and prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the hadith
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the hadith and its clarification by Imam Ghazali.
2
Analyze Ibn Kathir’s commentary
Notice how Ibn Kathir shows that negation of shirk implies tawhid and necessitates belief in prophethood.
3
Reflect on the wudu analogy
Consider how the analogy of wudu and prayer illustrates that non-association is necessary but insufficient without other conditions.

Source Text

وهو الاخلاص في العبادة لله سبحانه ، وإن اختلفت شرائعهم
سبحانه :

(۱)

وتحقيق التوحيد : هو معرفته والاطلاع على حقيقته ، والقيام بها علما وحقيقة ذلك هو انجذاب الروح إلى الله تعالى ، محبة ، وخوفا ، وإنابة ، وتوكلا ، ودعاء ، وإخلاصا ، واجلالا ، وهيبة ، وتعظيما وعبادة . وبالجملة : فلا يكون في قلبه شيء لغير الله سبحانه ، ولا إرادة لما حرم
الله ،
ولا كراهة لما أمر الله
وذلك هو حقيقة : «لا إله إلا الله » فإن الاله هو
المألوه المعبود وذلك هو حقيقة الشهادتين ، فمن قام بهما على هذا الوجه فهو من
الذين يدخلون الجنة
It is sincerity in worship of Allah Almighty, even if their laws differ.  He says: 'For each of you We have appointed a law and a way.' (1)  He says: And in His saying: 'And the right of the servants upon Allah is that He does not punish anyone who associates nothing with Him,' it is clarification that Allah does not punish the one who worships Him and associates nothing with Him, and that worship is performing commands and refraining from prohibitions, because mere non-association does not necessitate negation of punishment, and that is known from the Noble Qur'an and the noble hadiths that have come threatening the wrongdoers and sinners.  Imam al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir, may Allah have mercy on him, says: He limited it to negation of association because it necessitates tawhid by implication, and necessitates affirmation of prophethood by necessity, for whoever denies the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, has denied Allah Almighty, and whoever denies Allah is an associate (mushrik). It is like the saying: 'Whoever performs ablution, his prayer is valid' – meaning, along with the rest of the conditions. So the meaning is: whoever dies while being a believer in all that must be believed in, and practice.  And the realization of tawhid is: knowing it and being acquainted with its reality, and performing it in knowledge and practice. The reality of that is the attraction of the soul to Allah Almighty: love, fear, turning in repentance, trust, supplication, sincerity, veneration, awe, magnification, and worship. In summary: there should be nothing in his heart for other than Allah Almighty, no desire for what Allah has forbidden, and no hatred for what Allah has commanded. And that is the reality of 'There is no god but Allah' – for al-ilah (the god) is al-mā'lūh (the one worshipped). And that is the reality of the two testimonies. Whoever acts upon them in this manner is among those who enter Paradise.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered definition and explanation of tawhid. It begins by stating that tawhid is sincerity in worship, even though the specific laws of different prophets vary, citing Quran 5:48. Then it moves to a hadith about Allah's right over the servants: He will not punish those who do not associate anything with Him. The author clarifies that this does not mean mere non-association suffices; worship requires actively doing commands and avoiding prohibitions. The author then quotes Ibn Kathir, who explains that the hadith's focus on denying association implies tawhid and also necessitates belief in prophethood, since rejecting the messenger leads to disbelief. An analogy of wudu and prayer is given: just as wudu alone doesn't make prayer valid without other conditions, so too non-association alone doesn't guarantee salvation without fulfilling all obligations. The passage then defines the realization of tawhid as comprehensive knowledge and practice: the soul is attracted to Allah through various spiritual qualities like love, fear, trust, etc., leaving no room in the heart for anything other than Allah—no desire for the forbidden, no hatred for the commanded. Finally, it identifies this total devotion as the true meaning of 'La ilaha illa Allah', and whoever embodies both testimonies (shahadahayn) in this way will enter Paradise.

Key Terms
إخلاص (ikhlas)
توحيد (tawhid)
لا إله إلا الله (la ilaha illa Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that avoiding shirk alone guarantees salvation, regardless of other sins or obligations.
Correction: The passage clarifies that mere non-association does not negate punishment; worship requires performing commands and refraining from prohibitions. The hadith implies all conditions must be met.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the hadith's emphasis on negating shirk also require belief in prophethood?
A) Because prophets are messengers of tawhid
B) Because denying the Prophet is a form of shirk
C) Because the hadith mentions Muhammad explicitly
D) Because worship requires following a prophet

Key Takeaway
Tawhid demands not only avoiding shirk but actively fulfilling all acts of worship and believing in the Prophet; mere non-association is insufficient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever comforted yourself by saying 'at least I don't commit shirk' while neglecting your daily prayers or other obligations? How will you respond today to the true meaning of this hadith that demands full worship?
?
Ibn Kathir's analogy says that just as wudu alone doesn't make prayer valid without conditions, your avoidance of shirk doesn't save you without complete faith and practice. What is the one condition of worship you are most deficient in, and what concrete step will you take this week to strengthen it?
?
The hadith implies belief in prophethood is necessary. Do you truly follow the Prophet's sunnah in your life, or have you relegated his teachings to optional advice? If you examined your daily actions, what evidence is there that you believe in him as the final messenger?

The Reality of Tawhid: Total Devotion to Allah
Imam Ghazali defines the realization of tawhid and its practical manifestation.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
True tawhid is when your heart has nothing for anyone but Allah — love, fear, hope, and action all for Him.

After discussing the hadith, Imam Ghazali turns to the deeper meaning of tawhid. He defines its realization as knowing and embodying it, describing the soul's total orientation toward Allah. This lesson explores that inner reality and shows how it encapsulates the shahada.

1

وتحقيق التوحيد : هو معرفته والاطلاع على حقيقته ، والقيام بها علما وحقيقة ذلك هو انجذاب الروح إلى الله تعالى ، محبة ، وخوفا ، وإنابة ، وتوكلا ، ودعاء ، وإخلاصا ، واجلالا ، وهيبة ، وتعظيما وعبادة . وبالجملة : فلا يكون في قلبه شيء لغير الله سبحانه ، ولا إرادة لما حرم
الله ،

الذين يدخلون الجنة
It is sincerity in worship of Allah Almighty, even if their laws differ.  He says: 'For each of you We have appointed a law and a way.' (1)  He says: And in His saying: 'And the right of the servants upon Allah is that He does not punish anyone who associates nothing with Him,' it is clarification that Allah does not punish the one who worships Him and associates nothing with Him, and that worship is performing commands and refraining from prohibitions, because mere non-association does not necessitate negation of punishment, and that is known from the Noble Qur'an and the noble hadiths that have come threatening the wrongdoers and sinners.  Imam al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir, may Allah have mercy on him, says: He limited it to negation of association because it necessitates tawhid by implication, and necessitates affirmation of prophethood by necessity, for whoever denies the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, has denied Allah Almighty, and whoever denies Allah is an associate (mushrik). It is like the saying: 'Whoever performs ablution, his prayer is valid' – meaning, along with the rest of the conditions. So the meaning is: whoever dies while being a believer in all that must be believed in, and practice.  And the realization of tawhid is: knowing it and being acquainted with its reality, and performing it in knowledge and practice. The reality of that is the attraction of the soul to Allah Almighty: love, fear, turning in repentance, trust, supplication, sincerity, veneration, awe, magnification, and worship. In summary: there should be nothing in his heart for other than Allah Almighty, no desire for what Allah has forbidden, and no hatred for what Allah has commanded. And that is the reality of 'There is no god but Allah' – for al-ilah (the god) is al-mā'lūh (the one worshipped). And that is the reality of the two testimonies. Whoever acts upon them in this manner is among those who enter Paradise.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a multi-layered definition and explanation of tawhid. It begins by stating that tawhid is sincerity in worship, even though the specific laws of different prophets vary, citing Quran 5:48. Then it moves to a hadith about Allah's right over the servants: He will not punish those who do not associate anything with Him. The author clarifies that this does not mean mere non-association suffices; worship requires actively doing commands and avoiding prohibitions. The author then quotes Ibn Kathir, who explains that the hadith's focus on denying association implies tawhid and also necessitates belief in prophethood, since rejecting the messenger leads to disbelief. An analogy of wudu and prayer is given: just as wudu alone doesn't make prayer valid without other conditions, so too non-association alone doesn't guarantee salvation without fulfilling all obligations. The passage then defines the realization of tawhid as comprehensive knowledge and practice: the soul is attracted to Allah through various spiritual qualities like love, fear, trust, etc., leaving no room in the heart for anything other than Allah—no desire for the forbidden, no hatred for the commanded. Finally, it identifies this total devotion as the true meaning of 'La ilaha illa Allah', and whoever embodies both testimonies (shahadahayn) in this way will enter Paradise.

Key Terms
توحيد (tawhid)
لا إله إلا الله (la ilaha illa Allah)
شهادتين (shahadatayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawhid is only creedal belief, not affecting the heart and actions.
Correction: The passage states that realization of tawhid involves the soul's attraction to Allah through love, fear, etc., and that the heart should have nothing for other than Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'tahqiq al-tawhid' (realization of tawhid) involve?
A) Only knowing Allah's attributes
B) Attracting the soul to Allah through various states and emptying the heart for Him
C) Performing only the obligatory acts
D) Reciting the shahada with faith

Key Takeaway
The realization of tawhid is total devotion of the heart to Allah, exemplified by love, fear, trust, and worship, which is the true meaning of 'La ilaha illa Allah'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your heart honestly, is there any desire—for status, wealth, or a relationship—that competes with your love for Allah? What would it cost you to remove that from your heart as this passage demands?
?
You say 'La ilaha illa Allah' daily, but do you truly feel no hatred for what Allah commands and no desire for what He forbids? What specific command or prohibition are you struggling with right now?
?
The passage lists ten states of the soul: which one is most absent in your life—fear, hope, trust, sincerity? What step will you take today to cultivate that state?

The Hadith of 'Ubada: Conditions of Shahada
Hadith from 'Ubada listing required testimonies for Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific testimonies required by the hadith of 'Ubada for entry into Paradise and their significance as conditions of the shahada.

Core Idea
The shahada includes belief in Jesus as Allah's word and spirit.

The hadith from 'Ubada ibn al-Samit provides a comprehensive list of testimonies that form the conditions for entering Paradise. This lesson unpacks each element, showing that the shahada is not merely a verbal declaration but encompasses belief in the oneness of Allah, the prophethood of Muhammad, the special status of Jesus, and the realities of Paradise and Hell. By studying this hadith, we see the foundational beliefs that define the Muslim faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text
Read the hadith in Arabic carefully, then refer to the translation to ensure understanding of each component.
Notice the precise wording for Jesus: 'Abdullah, His word, and a spirit from Him.'
2
Identify the five testimonies
List the five distinct testimonies mentioned: Tawhid, Muhammad's prophethood, Jesus's status, truth of Paradise, truth of Hell.
These are the conditions for the promise of Paradise.
3
Examine the status of Jesus
Reflect on the triple description of Jesus: servant, messenger, word and spirit. This clarifies his role in Islam.
This distinguishes Islamic belief from both Judaism and Christianity.
4
Reflect on the phrase about deeds
Consider the phrase 'on whatever deed he has done.' This does not mean deeds are irrelevant, but that deeds are accepted on the foundation of correct belief.
A common misconception is that sins are automatically forgiven; rather, belief is the prerequisite.
5
Connect to the conditions of shahada
Understand that this hadith is presented as evidence for the required beliefs that constitute the full shahada, as discussed in the broader lesson.
This hadith is a key proof text for the conditions of faith (iman).

From 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: Whoever testifies that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, and that Jesus is the servant of Allah and His Messenger, and His word which He cast into Mary and a spirit from Him, and that Paradise is true, and that the Fire is true, Allah will admit him into Paradise on whatever deed he has done. (1) And how beautiful and splendid is this wonderful authentic hadith, encompassing the goods of this world and the Hereafter: At-Tirmidhi narrated in his Sunan from the hadith of al-Harith al-Ash'ari that the Prophet said: Allah commanded Yahya ibn Zakariya with five words to act upon and commanded the Children of Israel to act upon them, and he was about to delay them. So 'Isa, peace be upon him, said: Allah has commanded you with five words, so act upon them and command the Children of Israel to act upon them. Do you command them or shall I command them? Yahya, peace be upon him, said: I fear that if you precede me in it, I will be swallowed up or punished. So he gathered the people in Jerusalem, and it became full, and they sat on the elevated places, and he said: Allah commanded me with five words that I should act upon them and command you to act upon them: The first of them: that you worship Allah and associate nothing with Him, and the example of one who associates with Allah is like a man who bought a slave from his pure wealth with gold or silver, and he said: This...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents two companion hadiths as proofs of the conditions of the shahada. The first hadith (from 'Ubada) lists the essential testimonies: belief in the oneness of Allah, Muhammad's prophethood, Jesus's special status as servant and messenger, the Word and Spirit from Allah, and the reality of Paradise and Hell. The author adds an enthusiastic remark about the beauty of this hadith. The second hadith (from al-Harith al-Ash'ari) narrates a story about Yahya and 'Isa, where Yahya fears punishment if he delays, so he gathers the Children of Israel and commands them with five words. The first word is pure monotheism (worship Allah without association), and then an analogy: a master who bought a slave with his pure wealth but the slave attributes ownership to another – similar to the one who associates partners with Allah. The passage is cut off mid-analogy, but the point is clear: shirk is the ultimate betrayal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'on whatever deed he has done' means that good deeds are not necessary; belief alone saves regardless of sins.
Correction: The hadith sets the conditions for entry into Paradise, but deeds are still judged. The phrase indicates that belief is the foundation upon which deeds are accepted, not that sins are automatically forgiven without repentance or accountability.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of 'Ubada establishes that the shahada requires belief in Jesus as Allah's word and spirit, alongside Tawhid, Muhammad's prophethood, and the realities of Paradise and Hell.

?

?
This hadith promises Paradise based on faith. Is your faith built on these exact testimonies? Do you have any doubts about any of them?
?
The hadith says 'on whatever deed he has done' if the faith is correct. What deeds in your life are built on the foundation of this correct shahada?

The Prerequisites for Entering Paradise
Ghazali presents a hadith listing the conditions for entering Paradise and praises it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the essential beliefs that guarantee entry into Paradise according to a prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
Correct creed is the foundation; specific testimonies open the door to Paradise.

In this lesson, we explore a profound hadith that outlines the core beliefs a Muslim must hold to be promised Paradise. Imam al-Ghazali presents this narration from Ubadah ibn al-Samit, highlighting its beauty and comprehensiveness. The hadith emphasizes that salvation is tied to affirming the oneness of Allah, the prophethood of Muhammad and Jesus, and the reality of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1

The hadith is authentic and comprehensive.

Each testimony is a condition for entering Paradise.
3
Understand the significance of each

This hadith explicitly refutes shirk and innovation.
4
Appreciate the promise and conclusion
Note that the hadith says 'regardless of what deeds he did' — emphasizing that correct belief is the key, though deeds are still important.
Ghazali praises the hadith as beautiful and comprehensive.

From Ubadah ibn al-Samit, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: Whoever testifies that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and that Muhammad is His slave and His Messenger, and that Jesus is the slave of Allah and His Messenger, and His Word which He cast into Mary, and a Spirit from Him, and that Paradise is true, and that the Fire is true, Allah will admit him to Paradise regardless of what deeds he did. How beautiful and magnificent is this noble, authentic hadith, comprehensive of the goods of this world and the Hereafter.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith transmitted by Ubadah ibn al-Samit. The Prophet lists the essential testimonies and beliefs that guarantee entry into Paradise. First, the shahada of Tawheed (monotheism). Second, belief in Muhammad as Allah's slave and messenger. Third, belief in Jesus as Allah's slave, messenger, His Word cast into Mary, and a spirit from Him—affirming Jesus's created nature and prophethood, countering exaggerations. Fourth, belief in Paradise and Hell as true realities. The hadith concludes that whoever affirms these will enter Paradise regardless of his deeds—underscoring that correct creed is the foundation, and though deeds are important, they do not negate the promise for a believer. Ghazali then praises the hadith as beautiful and comprehensive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The hadith makes clear that specific beliefs are the prerequisites, and deeds follow; correct creed is the foundation.

Affirming these core beliefs ensures Paradise, regardless of deeds.

The Five Commands of Yahya: Worship and Remembrance
Yahya delivers five commands with analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five core commands that Allah gave to Yahya and the powerful analogies that illustrate their importance.

Core Idea
Five commands from Prophet Yahya—worship, prayer, fasting, charity, and remembrance—protect and purify the believer.

This passage presents a beautiful hadith where Prophet Yahya, urged by Jesus, gathers the Children of Israel and delivers five divine commands with striking analogies. Each command is accompanied by a vivid comparison that makes its spiritual benefit clear, from the folly of shirk to the power of dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of Yahya and Jesus
Notice the dialogue between Yahya and Jesus and how it led to the assembly.
2
Identify the five commands
List the five commands given by Yahya: Tawheed, prayer, fasting, charity, and remembrance.
3
Study the analogies
For each command, note the analogy given and reflect on its meaning.
4
Connect to your own practice
Consider how these commands and analogies relate to your own worship and daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخرج الترمذي في سننه من حديث الحارث الأشعري ، أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إن الله أمر يحيى بن زكريا بخمس كلمات أن يعمل بها ، وأمر بني اسرائيل أن يعملوا بها ، وإنه كان يبطئ بها فقال عيسى عليه السلام : إن الله أمرك بخمس كلمات فتعمل بها وتأمر بني اسرائيل أن يعملوا بها فإما أن تأمرهم وإما أن آمرهم فقال يحيى عليه السلام : أخشى إن سبقتني بها أن يخسف بي أو أعذب فجمع الناس في بيت المقدس فامتلأ وقعدوا على الشرف فقال : إن الله أمرني بخمس كلمات أن أعمل بهن وآمركم أن تعملوا بهن : أولهن : أن تعبدوا الله ولا تشركوا به شيئا وإن مثل من أشرك بالله كمثل رجل اشترى عبدا من خالص ماله بذهب أو ورق فقال هذه داري وهذا عملي فاعمل وأد إلي فكان يعمل ويؤدي إلى غير سيده فأيكم يرضى أن يكون عبده كذلك ؟ وإن الله أمركم بالصلاة فإذا صليتم فلا تلتفتوا فإن الله ينصب وجهه لوجه عبده في صلاته مالم يلتفت وأمركم بالصيام فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل في عصابة معه صرة فيها مسك فكلهم يعجب أو يعجبه ريحها وإن ريح الصائم أطيب عند الله من ريح المسك وأمركم بالصدقة فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل أسره العدو فأوثقوا يده على عنقه وقدموه ليضربوا عنقه فقال أنا أفديه منكم بالقليل والكثير ففدى نفسه منهم وأمركم أن تذكروا الله فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل خرج العدو في أثره سراعا حتى أتى على حصن حصين فأحرز نفسه منهم كذلك العبد لا يحرز نفسه من الشيطان إلا بذكر الله قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : وأنا آمركم بخمس الله أمرني بهن : السمع والطاعة والجهاد والهجرة والجماعة فإن من فارق الجماعة قيد شبر فقد خلع ربقة الإسلام من عنقه إلا أن يراجع ومن ادعى دعوى الجاهلية فإنه من حثاء جهنم فقال رجل يا رسول الله وإن صلى وصام ؟
Al-Tirmidhi narrated in his Sunan from the hadith of Al-Harith al-Ash'ari that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed Allah commanded Yahya ibn Zakariya with five words to act upon them, and He commanded the Children of Israel to act upon them, and he was delaying in them. So Jesus, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed Allah commanded you with five words, so act upon them and command the Children of Israel to act upon them. Either you command them or I command them." So Yahya, peace be upon him, said: "I fear that if you precede me in them, I will be swallowed up or punished." So he gathered the people in Jerusalem, and it was filled, and they sat on the raised areas, and he said: "Indeed Allah commanded me with five words that I act upon them and I command you to act upon them: The first of them: that you worship Allah and associate nothing with Him. And the example of the one who associates partners with Allah is like a man who bought a slave from his pure wealth with gold or silver, and said: This is my house, and this is my work, so work and deliver to me. The slave would work and deliver to someone other than his master. So which of you is pleased that his slave be like that? And indeed Allah commanded you with prayer: when you pray, do not turn aside, for Allah sets His face to the face of His slave in his prayer as long as he does not turn aside. And He commanded you with fasting: the example of that is like a man among a company with a pouch of musk in his possession, and all of them marvel or are pleased with its smell. And the smell of the fasting person is more pleasing to Allah than the smell of musk. And He commanded you with charity: the example of that is like a man captured by the enemy, so they tied his hands to his neck and brought him forward to strike his neck, and he said: 'I will ransom myself from you with little and much,' so he ransomed himself from them. And He commanded you to remember Allah: the example of that is like a man whose enemy pursued him swiftly until he came upon a fortified fortress and protected himself from them. Likewise, the slave does not protect himself from the devil except by remembrance of Allah.' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'And I command you with five that Allah commanded me with: hearing and obedience, jihad, hijra, and the community. For whoever separates from the community by a handspan has cast off the yoke of Islam from his neck, unless he returns. And whoever claims the claim of Jahiliyya, then he is among the fuel of Hell.' So a man said: 'O Messenger of Allah, even if he prays and fasts?'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a lengthy hadith narrating how Allah commanded Yahya ibn Zakariya with five important teachings for the Children of Israel. When Yahya hesitated, Jesus intervened, leading Yahya to gather the people and deliver the commands with vivid analogies. The five commands are: (1) Tawheed—worshipping Allah alone without shirk, illustrated by a slave who works for another master, showing how repulsive shirk is. (2) Prayer—performed with concentration, because Allah faces His servant as long as he does not turn away. (3) Fasting—its reward is more fragrant than musk to Allah. (4) Charity—likened to a captive ransoming himself, showing charity frees the giver from the punishment. (5) Remembrance of Allah—like seeking refuge in a fortress from a pursuing enemy; dhikr is the believer's fortress against Satan. The Prophet then adds five more commands he was given: hearing and obedience to authority, jihad (striving), hijra (migration), and sticking to the community (jama'ah). He warns that leaving the community even slightly removes the yoke of Islam, and that claiming pre-Islamic allegiances is fuel for Hell. The passage ends with a man asking if this applies even to one who prays and fasts, indicating the gravity of these communal obligations.

Key Terms
يحيى بن زكريا
عيسى
خمس كلمات
لا تشركوا به شيئا
الصلاة
الصيام
الصدقة
ذكر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that shirk is only about worshiping idols or other gods.
Correction: The analogy shows that shirk includes directing any act of worship or obedience to other than Allah, even if one outwardly claims to serve Allah.

Checkpoint
What analogy did Yahya give for the one who associates partners with Allah?
A) A slave who works for two masters
B) A slave who earns but delivers to someone other than his master
C) A slave who buys himself
D) A slave who refuses to work

Key Takeaway
The five commands of Yahya — Tawheed, prayer, fasting, charity, and remembrance — are essential acts of worship that protect and purify the believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The analogy for shirk is a slave who works for his master but delivers the earnings to someone else. Reflect on your daily deeds — your prayers, your work, your help to others. Are you truly delivering them to Allah alone, or is there a part of you that seeks the approval of people or the satisfaction of your own ego? What is one specific deed you will consciously redirect to be solely for Allah starting today?
?
Prophet Yahya feared the consequence of delaying the command. Is there any act of worship or obedience you know you should do but have been putting off? In what area of your life are you hesitating, and what small step can you take right now to overcome that delay before it leads to regret?
?
The fasting person's spiritual fragrance is better than musk to Allah. When you fast, do those around you smell the sweetness of your character — your patience, generosity, and self-restraint — or do they still encounter irritation and selfishness? What specific attitude change will you make in your next fast to make its scent more pleasing to your Creator?

The Prophet's Five Commands: Unity and Striving
Prophet Muhammad adds five commands with warnings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five commands given to Prophet Muhammad—hearing and obedience, jihad, hijra, and community—and the severe warning against abandoning the community.

Core Idea
The Prophet's five commands emphasize unity, obedience, and striving, warning that leaving the community even slightly endangers one's Islam.

After recounting Yahya's commands, the Prophet adds five more that Allah commanded him directly: hearing and obedience, jihad, hijra, and clinging to the community. He warns that separating from the community by even a handspan removes the yoke of Islam, and that claiming the call of Jahiliyyah places one in Hellfire, regardless of individual acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Prophet's additional commands
Focus on the five items: hearing and obedience, jihad, hijra, and community.
The list includes: hearing (السمع), obedience (الطاعة), jihad (الجهاد), hijra (الهجرة), and the community (الجماعة).
2
Understand the warning about the community
Note the strong warning: leaving the community by a handspan removes the yoke of Islam.
3
Reflect on the claim of Jahiliyya
Consider what it means to claim pre-Islamic allegiances and why it is so dangerous.
4
Answer the question at the end
Think about why the man asked 'even if he prays and fasts?' and what that implies about the importance of community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخرج الترمذي في سننه من حديث الحارث الأشعري ، أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إن الله أمر يحيى بن زكريا بخمس كلمات أن يعمل بها ، وأمر بني اسرائيل أن يعملوا بها ، وإنه كان يبطئ بها فقال عيسى عليه السلام : إن الله أمرك بخمس كلمات فتعمل بها وتأمر بني اسرائيل أن يعملوا بها فإما أن تأمرهم وإما أن آمرهم فقال يحيى عليه السلام : أخشى إن سبقتني بها أن يخسف بي أو أعذب فجمع الناس في بيت المقدس فامتلأ وقعدوا على الشرف فقال : إن الله أمرني بخمس كلمات أن أعمل بهن وآمركم أن تعملوا بهن : أولهن : أن تعبدوا الله ولا تشركوا به شيئا وإن مثل من أشرك بالله كمثل رجل اشترى عبدا من خالص ماله بذهب أو ورق فقال هذه داري وهذا عملي فاعمل وأد إلي فكان يعمل ويؤدي إلى غير سيده فأيكم يرضى أن يكون عبده كذلك ؟ وإن الله أمركم بالصلاة فإذا صليتم فلا تلتفتوا فإن الله ينصب وجهه لوجه عبده في صلاته مالم يلتفت وأمركم بالصيام فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل في عصابة معه صرة فيها مسك فكلهم يعجب أو يعجبه ريحها وإن ريح الصائم أطيب عند الله من ريح المسك وأمركم بالصدقة فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل أسره العدو فأوثقوا يده على عنقه وقدموه ليضربوا عنقه فقال أنا أفديه منكم بالقليل والكثير ففدى نفسه منهم وأمركم أن تذكروا الله فإن مثل ذلك كمثل رجل خرج العدو في أثره سراعا حتى أتى على حصن حصين فأحرز نفسه منهم كذلك العبد لا يحرز نفسه من الشيطان إلا بذكر الله قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : وأنا آمركم بخمس الله أمرني بهن : السمع والطاعة والجهاد والهجرة والجماعة فإن من فارق الجماعة قيد شبر فقد خلع ربقة الإسلام من عنقه إلا أن يراجع ومن ادعى دعوى الجاهلية فإنه من حثاء جهنم فقال رجل يا رسول الله وإن صلى وصام ؟
Al-Tirmidhi narrated in his Sunan from the hadith of Al-Harith al-Ash'ari that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed Allah commanded Yahya ibn Zakariya with five words to act upon them, and He commanded the Children of Israel to act upon them, and he was delaying in them. So Jesus, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed Allah commanded you with five words, so act upon them and command the Children of Israel to act upon them. Either you command them or I command them." So Yahya, peace be upon him, said: "I fear that if you precede me in them, I will be swallowed up or punished." So he gathered the people in Jerusalem, and it was filled, and they sat on the raised areas, and he said: "Indeed Allah commanded me with five words that I act upon them and I command you to act upon them: The first of them: that you worship Allah and associate nothing with Him. And the example of the one who associates partners with Allah is like a man who bought a slave from his pure wealth with gold or silver, and said: This is my house, and this is my work, so work and deliver to me. The slave would work and deliver to someone other than his master. So which of you is pleased that his slave be like that? And indeed Allah commanded you with prayer: when you pray, do not turn aside, for Allah sets His face to the face of His slave in his prayer as long as he does not turn aside. And He commanded you with fasting: the example of that is like a man among a company with a pouch of musk in his possession, and all of them marvel or are pleased with its smell. And the smell of the fasting person is more pleasing to Allah than the smell of musk. And He commanded you with charity: the example of that is like a man captured by the enemy, so they tied his hands to his neck and brought him forward to strike his neck, and he said: 'I will ransom myself from you with little and much,' so he ransomed himself from them. And He commanded you to remember Allah: the example of that is like a man whose enemy pursued him swiftly until he came upon a fortified fortress and protected himself from them. Likewise, the slave does not protect himself from the devil except by remembrance of Allah.' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'And I command you with five that Allah commanded me with: hearing and obedience, jihad, hijra, and the community. For whoever separates from the community by a handspan has cast off the yoke of Islam from his neck, unless he returns. And whoever claims the claim of Jahiliyya, then he is among the fuel of Hell.' So a man said: 'O Messenger of Allah, even if he prays and fasts?'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a lengthy hadith narrating how Allah commanded Yahya ibn Zakariya with five important teachings for the Children of Israel. When Yahya hesitated, Jesus intervened, leading Yahya to gather the people and deliver the commands with vivid analogies. The five commands are: (1) Tawheed—worshipping Allah alone without shirk, illustrated by a slave who works for another master, showing how repulsive shirk is. (2) Prayer—performed with concentration, because Allah faces His servant as long as he does not turn away. (3) Fasting—its reward is more fragrant than musk to Allah. (4) Charity—likened to a captive ransoming himself, showing charity frees the giver from the punishment. (5) Remembrance of Allah—like seeking refuge in a fortress from a pursuing enemy; dhikr is the believer's fortress against Satan. The Prophet then adds five more commands he was given: hearing and obedience to authority, jihad (striving), hijra (migration), and sticking to the community (jama'ah). He warns that leaving the community even slightly removes the yoke of Islam, and that claiming pre-Islamic allegiances is fuel for Hell. The passage ends with a man asking if this applies even to one who prays and fasts, indicating the gravity of these communal obligations.

Key Terms
السمع والطاعة
الجهاد
الهجرة
الجماعة
ربقة الإسلام
حثاء جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that individual acts of worship like prayer and fasting are sufficient for salvation regardless of communal ties.
Correction: The Prophet warns that even if one prays and fasts, abandoning the community or claiming Jahiliyya allegiances can lead to Hell.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say happens to the one who separates from the community by a handspan?
A) He is still a Muslim but sinners
B) He has cast off the yoke of Islam from his neck
C) He must repeat the shahada
D) He is forgiven if he prays

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's five commands highlight that communal unity, obedience, and striving are as essential as individual worship, and neglecting them can be spiritually fatal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel anger towards a fellow Muslim because of their tribe, nationality, or ethnicity, do you realize that you are committing the sin of Jahiliyya that the Prophet warned about? Will you repent and return to the bond of Islam instead of fueling the fire?
?
The Prophet warned that even a handspan of separation from the community can remove the yoke of Islam from your neck. In what practical ways are you distancing yourself from the Muslim community, and what steps will you take today to reconnect?
?
You may pray and fast regularly, but do you obey the legitimate Muslim authority? The Prophet commanded hearing and obedience as one of the five commands. Is there an area where you struggle to obey, and how will you surrender to Allah's command through the Prophet?

The Two Angels of the Grave: Munkar and Nakir
Al-Ghazali describes Munkar and Nakir and the grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the belief in the two angels Munkar and Nakir, their purpose in the grave, and the three fundamental questions they ask every soul.

Core Idea
Munkar and Nakir: the grave's examiners who test faith with three questions.

Imam al-Ghazali introduces a core belief of the Ahl al-Sunna: the questioning in the grave by two awesome angels. This passage establishes that after death, every soul is seated upright and asked about tawhid and risala. The angels are described as terrifying figures, and their questioning is the trial of the grave.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the names and description of the angels.
Notice the angels are called 'Munkar and Nakir' though only Nakir is named here.
2
Identify the three questions
Find the specific questions about Lord, religion, and Prophet. They cover tawhid and risala.
3
Understand the trial
Reflect on why this questioning is called a 'fitna' (trial) after death.
This connects to the iman in the unseen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونكير (1) وهما شخصان مهیبان هائلان (۲) ، يقعدان العبد في قبره (۳) سويا ، ذا روح وجسد (٤) ، فيسألانه عن التوحيد والرسالة (٥) ويقولان له من ربك وما دينك ومن نبيك ؟ وهما فتانا القبر ، وسؤالهما أو فتنة بعد الموت (٦) .
(۱) ويتقدم على ذلك وجوب إعتقاد أن ملك الموت يقبض روح كل ذي روح، أي يخرجها ويأخذها بإذن ربه من مقرها ، أو من أعوانه ، والمراد جميع أرواح الثقلين ، والملائكة والبهائم والطير وغيرهم ، ولو بعوضة ، حتى قيل : إنه يقبض روح نفسه
•
(۲) وهما شخصان أسودان أزرقان فظان غليظان شعورهما إلى أقدامهما تلمع النار بين أنيابهما يشكان الأرض بهما كلاهما كالرعد القاصف ، وأعينهما كالبرق الخاطف ، بأيديهما مقامع من حديد
(۳) يقعد ان العبد في قبره ، بعد تمام الدفن، وهذا في حق المقبور ، وفي غيره بعد الموت
(٤) علق الزبيدي على هذا بقوله :
ذا روح وجسد كامل الحواس » ، وأفتى الشمس الرملي : بأن السؤال على رأس وحده ، إن
