والكافرون » .
وورد في حق جماعة : أنهم لا يسألون ، كالمرابط، والشهيد بأنواعه ، والمراد به التخفيف لا
مطلقا
وفي سؤال الأطفال : الوقف ، وجزم السيوطي بعدم السؤال لعدم تكليفهم كالملائكة لا الجن
(٦) يحصل هذا السؤال في القبر ، وهو نفس الفتنة ، وهي الإختبار ، والإمتحان ، بالنظر إلى الميت ، أو إلينا ، أو إلى الملائكة لإحاطة عمله بكل شيء
And Nakir (1) and they are two awesome and terrifying figures (2), they sit the servant in his grave (3) upright, possessing spirit and body (4), and ask him about tawhid and risala (5) and say to him: 'Who is your Lord, what is your religion, and who is your Prophet?' They are the two examiners of the grave, and their questioning is the trial after death (6).
(1) And preceding that is the obligation to believe that the Angel of Death seizes every spirit, that is, he extracts it and takes it with his Lord's permission from its abode, or from his assistants, meaning all spirits of the two heavy groups (jinn and mankind), angels, beasts, birds, and others, even a mosquito, until it was said: he seizes his own spirit.
(2) They are two black, blue, harsh and cruel figures, their hair reaching to their feet, fire gleaming between their fangs, they pierce the earth with them, both like a thunderclap, their eyes like lightning flashes, in their hands iron maces.
(3) They sit the servant in his grave after the burial is complete, this is for the buried one, and for others after death.
(4) Al-Zabidi commented on this saying: 'possessing spirit and body, with complete senses', and al-Shams al-Ramli gave a fatwa: that the questioning is on the head alone if it is severed, due to the existence of evidence of speech.
And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti gave a fatwa: that if the deceased is moved, he is not questioned until he is buried.
(5) They ask him, or one of them; they are gentle with the believer, and severe with the hypocrite and disbeliever, even if his limbs are torn apart, or beasts have eaten him in their bellies, likewise the drowned and burnt even if his ashes are scattered in the wind. The questioning is about the Oneness of Allah Almighty, and the message of the prophets, peace be upon them, and what they conveyed. Imam al-Qurtubi has a valuable comment: 'The hadiths differ on the manner of questioning and answering according to persons; some are asked about some of their beliefs, others about all.'
Then the author of Ithaf al-Muttaqin comments: 'This questioning is specific to this ummah, meaning the ummah of the call, including believers, hypocrites, and disbelievers.'
And it has been reported concerning a group that they are not questioned, such as the one guarding the frontier, and the martyr in its various types, but this means mitigation not absolute exemption.
Concerning the questioning of children: there is suspension (waqf), and al-Suyuti firmly ruled no questioning due to their lack of obligation (taklif), like angels but not jinn.
(6) This questioning occurs in the grave, and it is the trial, the test, from the perspective of the deceased, or us, or the angels, because His knowledge encompasses everything.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage describes the questioning in the grave by the angels Munkar and Nakir. It begins by naming Nakir (the other angel named Munkar is implied from context) and describes them as terrifying figures. They sit the deceased upright in the grave and ask three fundamental questions: 'Who is your Lord?', 'What is your religion?', 'Who is your Prophet?' – testing tawhid and risala. The passage then provides extensive commentary (likely footnotes) covering several points: the prior belief in the Angel of Death who seizes all souls; a detailed physical description of the two angels as black and blue, with hair to the ground, fire between fangs, thunderous voices, lightning eyes, and iron maces; the timing of the questioning (after burial); fatwas by al-Zabidi, al-Ramli, and al-Suyuti on the survival of the body; the manner of questioning – gentle with believers, harsh with disbelievers; the scope of questioning (about tawhid and prophethood); al-Qurtubi's remark that questioning varies per person; a statement that this questioning is specific to the ummah of Prophet Muhammad; exceptions for martyrs and frontier guards (though only as mitigation); and a ruling on children (al-Suyuti says no questioning due to lack of taklif). The passage concludes that the grave questioning is the trial after death.

Key Terms
منكر ونكير
فتنة القبر
التوحيد
الرسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three questions asked by Munkar and Nakir according to this passage?
A) Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet?
B) What good deeds did you do? What is your name? Where did you come from?
C) Do you believe in Allah? Did you pray? Did you fast?
D) Who created you? What is your destiny? What is your final abode?

Key Takeaway
Munkar and Nakir are two angels who question every soul after death about tawhid and risala, and this questioning is the trial of the grave.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Munkar and Nakir were to question you right now about your Lord, your religion, and your Prophet, would your answers be based on certainty or mere habit? What is the one thing you will study this week to strengthen your conviction?
?
The angels are described as 'awesome and terrifying.' Do you feel fear at the thought of being questioned alone in your grave? If not, why? If yes, how will you use that fear to change your actions today?
?
You will be asked, 'Who is your Prophet?' – but do you truly know him? Commit to reading one hadith every night until you can answer with love and knowledge.

The Manner and Scope of the Grave Questioning
Al-Ghazali explains the timing, manner, and universality of the grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the timing of the grave questioning and how it is conducted—gentle for believers, harsh for disbelievers—and that it applies even in extreme circumstances.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is universal and unescapable: believers are treated gently, disbelievers harshly.

Having established the existence of Munkar and Nakir, Imam al-Ghazali now explains when and how the questioning occurs. The questioning begins immediately after burial for the buried, and after death for others. The angels are gentle with believers but severe with hypocrites and disbelievers, and no physical destruction exempts a soul from this trial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about timing and manner
Pay attention to when the questioning happens and how the angels behave.
2
Notice the universality
See that even if the body is torn apart or scattered, the questioning still occurs.
This shows the power of Allah over life and death.
3
Distinguish believers and disbelievers
Understand the difference in treatment: gentleness for believers, harshness for hypocrites and disbelievers.

(4) Al-Zabidi commented on this saying: 'possessing spirit and body, with complete senses', and al-Shams al-Ramli gave a fatwa: that the questioning is on the head alone if it is severed, due to the existence of evidence of speech.
And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti gave a fatwa: that if the deceased is moved, he is not questioned until he is buried.
(5) They ask him, or one of them; they are gentle with the believer, and severe with the hypocrite and disbeliever, even if his limbs are torn apart, or beasts have eaten him in their bellies, likewise the drowned and burnt even if his ashes are scattered in the wind. The questioning is about the Oneness of Allah Almighty, and the message of the prophets, peace be upon them, and what they conveyed. Imam al-Qurtubi has a valuable comment: 'The hadiths differ on the manner of questioning and answering according to persons; some are asked about some of their beliefs, others about all.'
Then the author of Ithaf al-Muttaqin comments: 'This questioning is specific to this ummah, meaning the ummah of the call, including believers, hypocrites, and disbelievers.'
And it has been reported concerning a group that they are not questioned, such as the one guarding the frontier, and the martyr in its various types, but this means mitigation not absolute exemption.
Concerning the questioning of children: there is suspension (waqf), and al-Suyuti firmly ruled no questioning due to their lack of obligation (taklif), like angels but not jinn.
(6) This questioning occurs in the grave, and it is the trial, the test, from the perspective of the deceased, or us, or the angels, because His knowledge encompasses everything.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage describes the questioning in the grave by the angels Munkar and Nakir. It begins by naming Nakir (the other angel named Munkar is implied from context) and describes them as terrifying figures. They sit the deceased upright in the grave and ask three fundamental questions: 'Who is your Lord?', 'What is your religion?', 'Who is your Prophet?' – testing tawhid and risala. The passage then provides extensive commentary (likely footnotes) covering several points: the prior belief in the Angel of Death who seizes all souls; a detailed physical description of the two angels as black and blue, with hair to the ground, fire between fangs, thunderous voices, lightning eyes, and iron maces; the timing of the questioning (after burial); fatwas by al-Zabidi, al-Ramli, and al-Suyuti on the survival of the body; the manner of questioning – gentle with believers, harsh with disbelievers; the scope of questioning (about tawhid and prophethood); al-Qurtubi's remark that questioning varies per person; a statement that this questioning is specific to the ummah of Prophet Muhammad; exceptions for martyrs and frontier guards (though only as mitigation); and a ruling on children (al-Suyuti says no questioning due to lack of taklif). The passage concludes that the grave questioning is the trial after death.

Key Terms
فتنة القبر
المنافق
الكافر
المؤمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only Muslims with a proper burial are questioned.
Correction: The passage states the questioning applies to all, including hypocrites and disbelievers, even if the body is destroyed.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how do the angels treat the believer during the grave questioning?
A) With severity
B) With gentleness
C) They ignore him
D) They ask only the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning occurs after death for all, with the angels being gentle to believers and severe to disbelievers, regardless of the body's condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live today as if you will be questioned in the grave by two angels who know your every secret? What would you change if you truly believed that moment is as certain as your next breath?
?
If your body were to be completely destroyed after death, do you believe your soul would still be held accountable? How does that certainty affect your actions right now, not just your beliefs?
?
The angels are gentle with believers and harsh with disbelievers. Based on your inner state, which treatment do you expect, and what are you actively doing today to deserve the gentle one?

Who is Questioned in the Grave? Exceptions and Rulings
Al-Ghazali discusses the scope of grave questioning and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the grave questioning applies to the entire ummah of the call, but some individuals like martyrs and frontier guards receive mitigation, and children are generally not questioned due to lack of taklif.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is universal for the ummah, but martyrs, frontier guards, and children are exceptions.

Imam al-Ghazali clarifies that the questioning in the grave is specific to the ummah of Prophet Muhammad, including believers, hypocrites, and disbelievers. However, certain individuals such as martyrs and those guarding the frontier may receive mitigation. For children, scholars differ, but al-Suyuti ruled they are not questioned due to not being obligated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the ummah of the call
Understand that the questioning is for the entire ummah that received the Prophet's message.
This includes believers, hypocrites, and disbelievers.
2
Note the exceptions
Martyrs and frontier guards are mentioned as those who may not be questioned, but this is mitigation.
Mitigation means they still face some judgment, but the questioning may be reduced.
3
Understand the ruling on children
Al-Suyuti's ruling that children are not questioned because they are not obligated (mukallaf).
Angels are also not questioned, but jinn are not included in this exception.

(۱) ويتقدم على ذلك وجوب إعتقاد أن ملك الموت يقبض روح كل ذي روح، أي يخرجها ويأخذها بإذن ربه من مقرها ، أو من أعوانه ، والمراد جميع أرواح الثقلين ، والملائكة والبهائم والطير وغيرهم ، ولو بعوضة ، حتى قيل : إنه يقبض روح نفسه

(۳) يقعد ان العبد في قبره ، بعد تمام الدفن، وهذا في حق المقبور ، وفي غيره بعد الموت

اختلفت الأحاديث في كيفية السؤال والجواب ، وذلك بحسب الأشخاص ، فمنهم من يسأل
عن بعض اعتقاداته ، ومنهم من يسأل عن كلها »
.
ثم يعلق على هذا صاحب اتحاف المتقين بشرح أسرار إحياء علوم الدين فيقول : وهذا السؤال خاص بهذه الأمة ، والمراد أمة الدعوة ، فيدخل المؤمنون ، والمنافقون ،
والكافرون » .
وورد في حق جماعة : أنهم لا يسألون ، كالمرابط، والشهيد بأنواعه ، والمراد به التخفيف لا
مطلقا
وفي سؤال الأطفال : الوقف ، وجزم السيوطي بعدم السؤال لعدم تكليفهم كالملائكة لا الجن
(٦) يحصل هذا السؤال في القبر ، وهو نفس الفتنة ، وهي الإختبار ، والإمتحان ، بالنظر إلى الميت ، أو إلينا ، أو إلى الملائكة لإحاطة عمله بكل شيء
And Nakir (1) and they are two awesome and terrifying figures (2), they sit the servant in his grave (3) upright, possessing spirit and body (4), and ask him about tawhid and risala (5) and say to him: 'Who is your Lord, what is your religion, and who is your Prophet?' They are the two examiners of the grave, and their questioning is the trial after death (6).
(1) And preceding that is the obligation to believe that the Angel of Death seizes every spirit, that is, he extracts it and takes it with his Lord's permission from its abode, or from his assistants, meaning all spirits of the two heavy groups (jinn and mankind), angels, beasts, birds, and others, even a mosquito, until it was said: he seizes his own spirit.
(2) They are two black, blue, harsh and cruel figures, their hair reaching to their feet, fire gleaming between their fangs, they pierce the earth with them, both like a thunderclap, their eyes like lightning flashes, in their hands iron maces.
(3) They sit the servant in his grave after the burial is complete, this is for the buried one, and for others after death.
(4) Al-Zabidi commented on this saying: 'possessing spirit and body, with complete senses', and al-Shams al-Ramli gave a fatwa: that the questioning is on the head alone if it is severed, due to the existence of evidence of speech.

(6) This questioning occurs in the grave, and it is the trial, the test, from the perspective of the deceased, or us, or the angels, because His knowledge encompasses everything.

The Belief in the Angel of Death
Al-Ghazali states the obligatory belief about the Angel of Death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that it is obligatory to believe that the Angel of Death seizes the souls of all living beings, including himself, by Allah's permission.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death seizes every soul, even his own.

Before detailing the grave questioning, Imam al-Ghazali emphasizes the prior obligation of believing in the Angel of Death. This angel takes every soul at the appointed time. The scope is all-encompassing: from humans and jinn to angels and even a mosquito. A remarkable report suggests he even takes his own soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Angel of Death
Understand the obligation to believe in this angel and his role.
This is the 'preceding' belief before the grave questioning.
2
Note the universality of soul-taking
All creatures, including angels and animals, are included.
3
Reflect on the final report
Consider the report that the Angel of Death takes his own soul.
This shows even the angel of death dies.

The Fate of the Believer Who Dies Without Verbalizing Faith
Al-Zabidi deduces salvation for the mute believer and discusses two views on deliberate silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly nuance about whether a person who has faith in their heart but dies without verbally professing it is saved, and the two opinions on the matter.

Core Idea
Death can excuse the utterance of faith, but deliberate silence requires interpretation.

Al-Zabidi presents a delicate theological question: what about someone who truly believes but never gets the chance to say the shahada before dying? He draws on a well-known hadith about removing from Hell those with even a mustard seed's weight of faith. This lesson unpacks his analysis of two scenarios and the implications for salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the distinction between the two cases: death prevents utterance vs. ability but deliberate omission. The hadith serves as evidence.
2
Understand al-Zabidi's deduction
Focus on the sentence: 'استنبط الزبيدي... نجاة من أيقن بالإيمان وحال بينه وبين النطق به الموت'. Why does he deduce salvation for the one prevented by death? What is the basis?
3
Analyze the two possibilities for the one who can speak but does not
The text presents two possibilities: one likening it to neglecting prayer (so not eternal in Hell), the other requiring a longer punishment. Which does the author favor? Why might this need interpretation (تأويل)?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي الصحيحين من حديث ابي سعيد رضي الله عنه : يدخل أهل الجنة الجنة ، وأهل النار النار ، ثم يقول الله تعالى : ( أخرجوا من كان في قلبه مثقال حبة من خردل من إيمان ) وقد استنبط الزبيدي من قوله تعالى: ﴿ وأخرجوا من كان الخ ) نجاة من أيقن بالإيمان وحال بينه وبين النطق به الموت ؛ أما من قدر على النطق ولم يفعل حتى مات مع إيقانه بالإيمان بقلبه فيحتمل أن يكون امتناعه منه بمنزلة إمتناعه عن الصلاة ، فلا يخلد في النار. ويحتمل خلافه، ورجح غيره الثاني فيحتاج الى تأويل ؛ ثم ينبغي أن يعلم أنه لا يشفع واحد ممن ذكر إلا بعد إنتهاء مدة المؤاخذة » اهـ
In the two Sahihs from the hadith of Abu Sa'id: 'The people of Paradise will enter Paradise, and the people of Hell will enter Hell, then Allah Almighty will say: "Bring out from it those who have in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of faith."' And al-Zabidi deduced from His statement 'and bring out those who have' that one who is certain of faith but death prevents him from uttering it (i.e., he dies mute) is saved. As for one who was able to utter it but did not until he died while having faith in his heart, it is possible that his refusal is like his refusal to pray, so he will not be eternal in Hell. It is also possible otherwise, and others favored the second opinion, so it requires interpretation. Then it should be known that none of those mentioned intercedes except after the term of punishment has ended.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage addresses a subtle theological issue: what about a person who has true faith in his heart but never verbally professes it before death? Al-Zabidi references the hadith about removing from Hell those with a mustard seed of faith. He deduces that if death prevents the person from uttering (e.g., he is mute or dies suddenly), he is undoubtedly saved. However, if he had the ability to speak but chose not to profess faith until death, there are two possibilities: one view equates it to neglecting prayer, so he might still not be eternal in Hell; another view (favored by others) suggests he might be punished longer. This is a point of interpretation. He concludes with a reminder that intercession only occurs after the period of punishment is over.

Key Terms
إيمان
نطق
مثقال حبة من خردل
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that verbal confession (shahada) is not necessary for salvation as long as one believes in the heart.
Correction: This passage shows that if one is able to speak, it is required; only death or inability excuses the utterance. Those who deliberately remain silent are subject to interpretation regarding their punishment.

Checkpoint
According to al-Zabidi, what is the ruling for one who dies immediately after believing but before being able to speak?
A) He is not saved because he did not confess.
B) He is saved because death prevented him.
C) He must be punished for neglect.
D) It depends on his deeds.

Key Takeaway
One who believes in the heart but dies before being able to utter the shahada is saved, while deliberate silence requires interpretation and may entail punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have the ability to openly declare your faith but remain silent out of fear or convenience, what does that say about the weight of your faith compared to the mustard seed mentioned in this hadith? Will you consciously utter the shahada this week in a situation where you normally shrink?
?
If the Prophet (saw) intercedes for believers only after they have undergone punishment, how does that challenge your assumption of an easy path to Paradise? What single sin, if punished, would you want to remove now through sincere repentance so that intercession is not your only hope?
?
The mute believer is saved because death prevented speech. You are not mute. So what excuse do you have for not speaking the truth when you should? Write one specific situation this week where you will verbally invite someone to good or defend your faith, and commit to it right now.

Conclusion: The People of Truth Cling to Transmitted Reports
Ghazali concludes that belief in transmitted reports defines Ahl al-Haqq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that correct belief is defined by certainty in transmitted reports, which distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from the people of innovation.

Core Idea
Certainty in transmitted reports defines the people of truth.

This concluding passage from Imam al-Ghazali ties together the entire discussion of belief. He makes clear that the foundation of correct aqidah is not rational speculation but firm conviction in what the Prophet and early Muslims conveyed. This lesson examines his final exhortation and what it means to be from Ahl al-Haqq.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow from the statement about reports to the definition of the people of truth and the supplication.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.

This connects certainty to the concept of thabat (steadfastness) in religion.

فكل ذلك مما وردت به الأخبار وشهدت به الآثار فمن اعتقد جميع ذلك موقنا كان من أهل الحق وعصابة السنة وفارق رهط الضلال وحزب البدعة فنسأل الله كمال اليقين وحسن الثبات في الدين لنا ولكافة المسلمين برحمته أنه أرحم الراحمين وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد وعلى كل عبد مصطفى

And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and every chosen servant.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This is a concluding passage from Imam al-Ghazali summarizing the foundation of correct belief. He states that everything he has mentioned in previous pages comes from transmitted reports (akhbar) and traditions (athar) of the early Muslims. Whoever holds these beliefs with firm certainty is considered from the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) and the party of the Sunnah (the followers of the Prophet's way). Such a person separates from the groups of misguidance and innovation (ahl al-bid'ah). Then Ghazali makes a supplication to Allah for complete certainty and good steadfastness in the religion for himself and all Muslims. He ends with salawat on the Prophet Muhammad and every chosen servant. This passage reinforces that the source of correct aqidah is the transmitted texts, and that certainty in them distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from the sects.

Three States of Simple Believers
Ghazali categorizes three states of believers lacking theological depth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's classification of believers who lack detailed theological knowledge into three categories and the rulings associated with each.

Core Idea
Simple faith can be valid even without deep theological knowledge.

Imam al-Ghazali addresses a delicate question: what about believers who accept the faith but lack detailed understanding of theological doctrines? He classifies such people into three categories, showing that Islam accommodates simple faith alongside scholarly knowledge. This passage is crucial for understanding the scope of faith and the limits of takfir.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three states
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Look for the three states described by Ghazali: (1) believing all pillars by taqlid, (2) believing only some pillars, (3) believing with some errors but not outright disbelief.
The passage is incomplete; focus on the three states as given.
2
Understand the ruling for each state
Note how Ghazali rules: first state is saved; second state is not excluded by early Salaf; third state is misguidance but not kufr.
3
Reflect on the practical implications
Consider why Ghazali gives leniency to simple believers. Think about the historical context of early converts.
This connects to the broader theme of balance in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم ينفتح له غيرها (۱) ، ولكنه يسلم في الآخرة بإعتقاد أهل الحق (٢) ، إذا لم يكلف الشرع أجلاف العرب أكثر من التصديق الجازم بظاهر هذه العقائد ، فأما البحث والتفتيش ، وتكلف نظم الأدلة فلم يكلفوه أصلا (٣) . وإن أراد أن يكون من (۱) كالتجارة والفلاحة وغيرهما من الصنائع والحرف ، لم ينفتح له غيرها ، لعدم انتقاله منها إلى حالة أخرى منها (۲) وفي نسخة أخرى : بإعتقاد الحق . والمراد أنه سلم في الآخرة عن المؤاخذة والمعاتبة بإعتقاده الحق المطابق للواقع ، كما أشار إلى ذلك غير واحد من الأئمة (۳) ومن شاهد أحوال الأولين انكشف له الأمر ، يقول الإمام الغزالي رضي الله عنه في كتاب الإملاء : إن أهل الإعتقاد المجرد عن تحصينه بالعلم وتوثيقه بالأدلة ، ينقسمون من وجه على ثلاث حالات : الأولى : أن يعتقد أحدهم جميع أركان الإيمان على ما يكمل عليه في الغالب ، لكنه على طريق التقليد الثانية : أن لا يعتقد إلا بعض الأركان مما فيه خلاف ، إذا انفرد ولم ينضف إليه من إعتقاده سواه ، هل يكون به مؤمناً أو مسلما، مثل أن يعتقد وجود الواحد فقط ، أو يعتقد أنه موجود حي لا غير ، وأمثال هذه التقريرات ، ويخلو عن إعتقاد باقي المصنفات خلواً كاملاً لا يعتقد فيها حقاً ولا باطلاً الثالثة : أن يعتقد الوجود كما قلناه ، أو الوجود والوحدانية ، والحياة، وفي باقي الصفات ، على ما لا يوافق الحق بما هو بدعة أو ضلالة ، وليس بكفر صراح : والذي يدل عليه العلم ، ويستنبط من ظواهر الشرع، أن أرباب الحالة الأولى على سبيل نجاة ، ووصف إيمان وإسلام ، وأما أهل الحالة الثانية : فالمتقدمون من السلف لم يشتهر عنهم في صورة هذه المسألة ما يخرج صاحب هذه العقيدة عن حكم الإيمان والإسلام . والمتأخرون مختلفون ، وكثير خاف أن يخرج من إعتقاد وجود الله تعالى ، وإظهار الإقرار به ونبيه من الإسلام ، ولا يبعد أن يكون كثير ممن أسلم من الأجلاف والرعيات ، وضعفاء النساء والإتباع ، هذا عقده بلا مزيد عليه . ولو سئلوا واستكشفوا عن الله عز وجل ، هل له إرادة ، أو كلام ، أو بقاء ، أو ما شاكل ذلك ؟ وهل له صفات معنوية ليست هي هو ، ولا هي غيره ، ربما وجدوا يجهلون ذلك ولا يعقلون وجه ما يخاطبون به ، وكيف يخرج من إعتقد وجود الله تعالى ، ووحدانيته تعالى ، مع الإقرار بالنبوة من
No other [occupation] opened for him (1), but he will be safe in the Hereafter with the belief of the people of truth (2), since the Law did not charge the coarse Arabs with more than firm affirmation of the apparent meaning of these articles of faith. As for investigation, scrutiny, and the burden of organizing proofs, they were not charged with that at all (3). And if he wanted to be among... (1) such as trade, agriculture, and other crafts and professions, no other opened for him, because he does not transition from them to another state. (2) In another copy: 'with the belief of truth.' The meaning is that he is safe in the Hereafter from being taken to task and reproached due to his belief in the truth that corresponds to reality, as more than one of the imams indicated. (3) And whoever observes the states of the early ones, the matter becomes clear to him. Imam Ghazali, may Allah be pleased with him, said in the book al-Imla': 'Indeed, the people of belief that is bare of being fortified by knowledge and strengthened by proofs are divided from one perspective into three states: First: that one of them believes all the pillars of faith as they are generally completed, but in the way of taqlid. Second: that he believes only some of the pillars concerning which there is disagreement, if he is isolated and his belief is not mixed with anything else, whether he is thereby a believer or a Muslim? For example, he believes in the existence of the One only, or believes that He is existent and living and nothing else, and similar formulations, and he is completely devoid of belief in the remaining attributes, not believing in them as true or false. Third: that he believes in existence as we said, or existence and oneness and life, and regarding the remaining attributes, he believes in a way that does not correspond to the truth, being an innovation or misguidance, but not outright disbelief. And what is indicated by knowledge and derived from the apparent meanings of the Law is that the people of the first state are on the path of salvation, and are described as having faith and Islam. As for the people of the second state: the early Salaf are not known to have ruled on this issue that such a person leaves the ruling of faith and Islam. The later scholars differed: many feared that such a person would leave Islam due to his belief in the existence of Allah and professing Him and His Prophet; but it is not unlikely that many of those who became Muslim from the coarse Bedouins, the common folk, and weak women and followers have this belief without more. And if they were asked and questioned about Allah, may He be glorified: does He have will, speech, permanence, or the like? Does He have essential attributes that are not Him and not other than Him? perhaps they would be found ignorant of that and not understand how to respond. And how can someone who believes in the existence of Allah the Exalted and His oneness, along with professing prophethood, be removed from...'
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a classification of believers based on their knowledge and belief. It begins with a discussion of a person for whom only certain occupations are possible, but he will be saved in the Hereafter due to his belief in the truth, because the Law (shar‘) did not require more than firm affirmation of the apparent meaning of the articles of faith from the simple Arabs. Then Ghazali quotes from his own book al-Imla’ to delineate three states of belief that are bare of being fortified by knowledge and proofs. The first state: believing all pillars of faith by taqlid (imitation). The second: believing only some pillars, such as existence and life, but not others—whether such a person is considered a believer is disputed. The third: believing in existence and oneness and life but holding incorrect beliefs about the remaining attributes, which are innovations but not outright disbelief. Ghazali then gives the ruling: the first state is saved and is described as faith and Islam. For the second state, the early Salaf did not explicitly exclude such a person from Islam, but later scholars differed. Many fear that holding only belief in existence and oneness without more might lead to exclusion, but Ghazali notes that many early converts from the Bedouins and common folk had exactly such limited belief. The passage ends with a rhetorical question: how can someone who believes in Allah and His oneness and professes prophethood be removed from Islam? The passage is incomplete but clearly argues for leniency in judging the faith of simple believers who lack detailed theological knowledge.

تقليد
أركان الإيمان
بدعة
ضلالة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that a believer must have detailed theological knowledge to be saved.
Correction: Ghazali shows that simple belief in the fundamentals by taqlid is sufficient for salvation, and partial belief without denial may also be within Islam.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the ruling for someone in the first state, who believes all pillars of faith by taqlid?
A) They are not considered believers
B) They are on the path of salvation and described as having faith and Islam
C) They are considered disbelievers
D) They are required to perform additional acts of worship

Key Takeaway
Simple believers who affirm the fundamentals of faith by taqlid are considered believers, and the early community did not exclude those with limited belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that simple, imitative faith is accepted by Allah. But reflect on your own heart: Do you rely on taqlid even when you have the ability to seek deeper knowledge? Is your faith merely inherited, or have you personally affirmed the essentials? What step can you take today to move from blind imitation to a more grounded conviction?
?
Ghazali describes people who believe in Allah's existence and oneness but are ignorant about His attributes—and yet he does not exclude them from Islam. Do you ever look down on others whose understanding of Islam is simpler or less detailed than yours? What does this lesson teach you about mercy and refraining from takfir (declaring others disbelievers)?
?
Imagine you were asked by someone with a simple faith: 'Does Allah have a will? Does He speak? How can I know?' Would you be able to answer them based on knowledge, or would you stumble? This lesson reveals that the early converts were not burdened with proofs. What does that reveal about Allah's mercy? And what does it demand from you in terms of humbly teaching others without overburdening them?

The Two Paths of Faith: Basic Belief and Striving for Higher Knowledge
Ghazali explains two levels of faith and the legal sufficiency of the Shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islam recognizes two levels of faith: a basic faith of firm assent sufficient for salvation and a higher faith attained through spiritual struggle, and that the Law does not require detailed theological knowledge from the common people.

Core Idea
Faith has two levels: basic acceptance and deep realization through struggle.

Imam al-Ghazali addresses a key question: what is the minimum required for faith? He distinguishes between the simple faith of the early Arabs and the deeper faith of the righteous. This passage explains that while the Law does not burden the common person with theological proofs, those who seek higher knowledge must engage in spiritual discipline. It also clarifies that uttering the Shahada sincerely is enough to enter Paradise, avoiding harsh judgments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two categories of believers
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Ghazali first discusses the crude Arabs, then those who tread the path of the Hereafter, and finally the legal judgment based on the Shahada.
The passage is continuous but has clear shifts in topic.
2
Understand why the crude Arabs were not required to study theology
Ghazali states that the Law only required firm assent (tasdiq jazim) to the apparent meaning, not research or proof construction. This shows that detailed knowledge is not obligatory for everyone.
This is a key point to avoid extremism.
3
Explore the higher path of spiritual struggle
For those who wish to attain higher levels, Ghazali describes engaging in action, piety, self-restraint, and spiritual struggle, which leads to divine guidance and unveiling of realities.
This path is associated with the 'secret' of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.
4
Reflect on the legal judgment: the Shahada is sufficient for salvation
Ghazali argues that the Prophet made the Shahada the criterion for entry into Paradise. The early converts only knew basic obligations, and it would be wrong to condemn them for lacking deeper theological knowledge.
This warns against declaring others as disbelievers.
5
Avoid the misconception that detailed theological knowledge is mandatory for all
The common misunderstanding is that every believer must master theology. Ghazali clearly differentiates between the common person's duty and the seeker's aspiration.
This lesson promotes tolerance and balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم ينفتح له غيرها ، ولكنه يسلم في الآخرة بإعتقاد أهل الحق ، إذا لم يكلف الشرع أجلاف العرب أكثر من التصديق الجازم بظاهر هذه العقائد ، فأما البحث والتفتيش ، وتكلف نظم الأدلة فلم يكلفوه أصلا . وإن أراد أن يكون من سالكي طريق الآخرة ، وساعده التوفيق ، حتى اشتغل بالعمل ، ولازم التقوى ، ونهى النفس عن الهوى ، واشتغل بالرياضة والمجاهدة ، انفتحت له أبواب من الهداية ، تكشف عن حقائق هذه العقيدة ، بنور الهي يقذف في قلبه بسبب المجاهدة تحقيقا لوعده عز وجل إذ قال : وَالَّذِينَ جَاهَدُواْ فِينَا لَنَهْدِيَنَّهُمْ سُبُلَنَا وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ لَمَعَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ وهو الجوهر النفيس الذي هو غاية إيمان الصديقين والمقربين ، وإليه الإشارة بالسر الذي وقر في صدر أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه ، حيث فضل به الخلق . وهيئات حكم الإسلام ، والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قد رفع القتال والقتل عنهم ، فأوجب حكم الإيمان والإسلام لمن قال : لا إله إلا الله ، وعقد عليها ؛ وهذه الكلمة لا تقتضي أكثر من إعتقاد الوجود والوحدة في الظاهر وعلى البديهة من غير نظر ؛ ثم سمعنا عمن قالها في صدر الإسلام ولم يعلم بعدها إلا فرائض الوضوء والصلاة ، الأعمال البدنية ، والكف عن أذى المسلم ؛ ولم يبلغنا أنهم تدارسوا علم الصفات وأحوالها ، ولأهل الله عالم بعلم ، أو عالم بنفسه ، أو هو باق ببقاء ، أو بنفسه ، وأشباه هذه المعارف ولا يدفع ظهور هذا إلا معاند أو جاهل بسيرة السلف ، وما جرى بينهم ، ويدل على قوة هذا الجانب في الشرع أن من استكشف منه على هذه الحالة وتحققت منه وأبى أن يذعن إلى تعلم ما زاد على ما عنده ، لم يفت أحد بقتله ولا باسترقاقه ، والحكم عليه بالخلود في النار ، عسير جداً وخطر عظيم ، مع ثبوت الشرع، بأن من قال : « لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة » اهـ
No other path opens for him, but he is saved in the Hereafter by believing the truth of Ahl al-Haqq, since the Law did not charge the crude Arabs with more than firm assent to the apparent [meaning] of these beliefs. As for investigation, scrutiny, and the effort of constructing proofs, they were not charged with it at all. But if he wishes to be among those who tread the path of the Hereafter, and divine success aids him, so that he occupies himself with action, adheres to piety, restrains his soul from passion, and occupies himself with spiritual discipline and struggle, there open for him doors of guidance that unveil the realities of this creed through a divine light cast into his heart because of his struggle, fulfilling His promise — Exalted is He — when He said: “And those who strive in Us, We will surely guide them to Our ways, and indeed Allah is with the doers of good.” And it is the precious jewel that is the ultimate goal of the faith of the truthful ones and the near ones, and it is what is indicated by the secret that settled in the chest of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him), through which he surpassed creation. And the judgments of Islam — the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) raised fighting and killing from them, so he made the judgment of faith and Islam binding for whoever says “There is no god but Allah” and contracts upon it. This word does not require more than belief in existence and oneness outwardly and intuitively without reflection. Then we have heard of those who said it in the early days of Islam and knew after it only the obligatory duties of ablution and prayer, physical acts, and refraining from harming a Muslim; and it has not reached us that they studied the science of attributes and their states, nor whether Allah has a knower by knowledge, or a knower by Himself, or whether He is everlasting by subsistence or by Himself, and similar cognitions. And none denies the obviousness of this except an obstinate person or one ignorant of the conduct of the Salaf and what occurred among them. It indicates the strength of this aspect in the Law that if someone is examined and found to be in this state and refuses to learn what is beyond what he has, no one has given a verdict to kill him or enslave him, and judging him to be eternally in the Fire is very difficult and a great danger, given the established Law that whoever says “There is no god but Allah” enters Paradise.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the sufficiency of basic faith for the common people and the higher path of realized faith. The author, Imam Ghazali, begins by stating that for the crude Arabs (ajlaf al-Arab), the Law did not require them to go beyond firm assent (tasdiq jazim) to the apparent meanings of the creed. They were not charged with research, scrutiny, or constructing proofs. However, if a person wishes to be among those seeking the Hereafter and is granted success, he engages in action, piety, self-restraint, and spiritual struggle (riyada and mujahada). Then doors of guidance open, unveiling the realities of the creed through a divine light cast into the heart — fulfilling God's promise in Quran 29:69. This is the precious jewel that is the ultimate faith of the truthful (siddiqin) and the near ones (muqarrabin), alluded to by the secret in the chest of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, through which he excelled. The passage then shifts to the legal judgment: the Prophet raised fighting and killing from those who say 'La ilaha illa Allah' and contract upon it. This word only requires belief in existence and oneness outwardly and intuitively (ala al-badiha). The early converts only knew the basic obligations; they did not study the science of attributes. It would be extreme to declare such a person an unbeliever or to condemn them to eternal fire, as the Law firmly states that whoever says 'La ilaha illa Allah' enters Paradise.

Key Terms
تصديق جازم
رياضة
مجاهدة
سر أبي بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Detailed theological knowledge is obligatory for all believers.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies that the Law only requires firm assent (tasdiq jazim) to the apparent meaning for the common people; research and proof construction are not obligatory for them.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the minimum requirement for faith for the crude Arabs?
A) To have detailed knowledge of God's attributes
B) To engage in research and construct proofs
C) To give firm assent (tasdiq jazim) to the apparent meaning of the beliefs
D) To perform spiritual exercises and struggle

Key Takeaway
Faith has two levels: basic acceptance is sufficient for salvation, but deeper realization requires spiritual struggle.

?

Three States of Bare Belief in Ghazali's Classification
Ghazali classifies believers with bare belief into three states and discusses their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's threefold classification of believers who lack detailed theological knowledge and the implications for their faith status.

Core Idea
Not all deficient belief is disbelief; Ghazali distinguishes three states.

Imam al-Ghazali, in his Kitab al-Imla, addresses a crucial pastoral and theological question: what about those who believe the essentials of the faith but lack detailed knowledge of its proofs or even some specific attributes? He identifies three distinct states, showing that salvation is not limited to the scholarly elite. This passage helps us appreciate the mercy and breadth of Islamic theology toward those with limited understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the classification and rulings.
2
Identify the three states
List the three states as described by Ghazali. Note the defining features of each.
The first is taqlid-based, the second is partial belief, the third is erroneous but not kufr.
3
Reflect on the rulings
Consider how the early Salaf and later scholars differ regarding the second state. Ask yourself: why does Ghazali mention the example of simple believers?
This connects to the broader theme of faith being valid even without detailed knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقول الإمام الغزالي رضي الله عنه في كتاب الإملاء : إن أهل الإعتقاد المجرد عن تحصينه بالعلم وتوثيقه بالأدلة ، ينقسمون من وجه على ثلاث حالات : الأولى : أن يعتقد أحدهم جميع أركان الإيمان على ما يكمل عليه في الغالب ، لكنه على طريق التقليد . الثانية : أن لا يعتقد إلا بعض الأركان مما فيه خلاف ، إذا انفرد ولم ينضف إليه من إعتقاده سواه ، هل يكون به مؤمناً أو مسلما، مثل أن يعتقد وجود الواحد فقط ، أو يعتقد أنه موجود حي لا غير ، وأمثال هذه التقريرات ، ويخلو عن إعتقاد باقي المصنفات خلواً كاملاً لا يعتقد فيها حقاً ولا باطلاً . الثالثة : أن يعتقد الوجود كما قلناه ، أو الوجود والوحدانية، والحياة، وفي باقي الصفات ، على ما لا يوافق الحق بما هو بدعة أو ضلالة ، وليس بكفر صراح . والذي يدل عليه العلم ، ويستنبط من ظواهر الشرع، أن أرباب الحالة الأولى على سبيل نجاة ، ووصف إيمان وإسلام ، وأما أهل الحالة الثانية : فالمتقدمون من السلف لم يشتهر عنهم في صورة هذه المسألة ما يخرج صاحب هذه العقيدة عن حكم الإيمان والإسلام . والمتأخرون مختلفون ، وكثير خاف أن يخرج من إعتقاد وجود الله تعالى ، وإظهار الإقرار به ونبيه من الإسلام ، ولا يبعد أن يكون كثير ممن أسلم من الأجلاف والرعيات ، وضعفاء النساء والإتباع ، هذا عقده بلا مزيد عليه . ولو سئلوا واستكشفوا عن الله عز وجل ، هل له إرادة ، أو كلام ، أو بقاء ، أو ما شاكل ذلك ؟ وهل له صفات معنوية ليست هي هو ، ولا هي غيره ، ربما وجدوا يجهلون ذلك ولا يعقلون وجه ما يخاطبون به ، وكيف يخرج من إعتقد وجود الله تعالى ، ووحدانيته تعالى ، مع الإقرار بالنبوة
Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah be pleased with him) says in the Book of al-Imla: Indeed, the people of bare belief, without fortifying it with knowledge and confirming it with proofs, are divided from one aspect into three states: The first: that one of them believes in all the pillars of faith as is generally complete, but in the way of taqlid. The second: that he believes only some of the pillars concerning which there is disagreement, when isolated and nothing else of his belief is added to it — whether he is thereby a believer or a Muslim — such as believing in existence of the One only, or believing that He is existent, living, and nothing else, and similar formulations, and he is completely devoid of belief in the remaining categories, believing neither truth nor falsehood about them. The third: that he believes in existence as we said, or existence and oneness, and life, and concerning the remaining attributes, in a way that does not accord with the truth, being an innovation or error, but not outright disbelief. And what knowledge indicates and is deduced from the apparent meanings of the Law is that the people of the first state are on the path of salvation, and are described with faith and Islam. As for the people of the second state: the early Salaf did not become known in the form of this issue to have excluded the possessor of this creed from the ruling of faith and Islam. The later scholars differ, and many feared that [such a person] would be excluded from Islam based on belief in the existence of Allah, manifesting affirmation of Him and His Prophet — and it is not unlikely that many of those who embraced Islam from among the crude, the rabble, the weak women, and the followers have this as their creed without more. And if they were asked and examined about Allah Almighty: Does He have will, or speech, or subsistence, or the like? Does He have attributes of meaning that are not He and not other than He? Perhaps they would be found ignorant of that and not understand the point of what they are addressed with. And how can one who believes in the existence of Allah Almighty and His oneness along with affirmation of prophethood be excluded [from Islam]?
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a classification of believers based on their relation to detailed knowledge and proofs, quoted from Ghazali's Kitab al-Imla. Ghazali states that those whose belief is bare (mujarrad) — not fortified with knowledge or confirmed by proofs — fall into three states. The first state: they believe all the pillars of faith in a complete manner but through taqlid (uncritical acceptance). The second state: they believe only some pillars, e.g., only that God exists, or that He is living, but they hold no belief at all about other categories — neither true nor false. The third state: they believe in some attributes but in a way that is incorrect (innovation or error) but not outright disbelief (kufr sarih). Ghazali then derives the ruling from knowledge and the apparent meanings of the Law: the first state leads to salvation and is considered faith and Islam. For the second state, the early Salaf did not rule out such a person from faith and Islam; later scholars differ, but many feared excluding someone who affirms God's existence and the Prophet. He notes that many crude Arabs, rabble, weak women, and followers had exactly this minimal creed. He rhetorically asks: if such a person is asked about detailed attributes like will, speech, etc., they would be ignorant, but how can one who believes in God's existence and oneness and affirms prophethood be excluded from Islam?

Key Terms
تقليد
بدعة
ضلالة
كفر صراح
أركان الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any deficiency in detailed theological knowledge makes one a non-Muslim.
Correction: Ghazali shows that early Salaf did not exclude those with minimal belief (second state) from faith, and erroneous but not outright kufr beliefs (third state) are not automatically disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali's classification, what is the second state of bare belief?
A) Believing all pillars via taqlid
B) Believing only some pillars and being completely ignorant of the rest, holding neither truth nor falsehood about them
C) Believing in existence and oneness but with erroneous details that amount to innovation
D) Rejecting the prophethood

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's classification demonstrates that faith can be valid with varying degrees of knowledge, and only specific erroneous beliefs (kufr sarih) exclude from Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to be asked about God's attributes like will, speech, and subsistence, would you be able to give a correct answer? Or are you in the second state of bare belief? What steps will you take to move from taqlid to knowledge?
?
Ghazali said that many early Muslims had a minimal creed yet were not excluded from Islam. Does your own certainty of faith rest on actual knowledge and proofs, or is it merely inherited? And if it is only inherited, are you content to remain in the first state?
?
When you hear of a Muslim who holds an erroneous belief about God's attributes, do you immediately question their Islam? How does Ghazali's classification challenge your tendency to judge others' faith?

Simple Faith Suffices: Al-Ghazali on the Shahada
Al-Ghazali argues simple faith suffices without detailed theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Ghazali's argument that a simple, intuitive faith in Allah's existence and oneness is sufficient for salvation, without requiring detailed theological knowledge.

Core Idea
Simple faith in Allah's oneness is enough; detailed theology is not required.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali addresses a key question: what is the minimum required for faith? Drawing on the practice of the Prophet and early Muslims, he argues that the simple declaration of 'There is no god but Allah' is sufficient, even without deep theological study. This challenges those who claim that detailed knowledge of God's attributes is necessary for salvation. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the central claim Al-Ghazali makes about the declaration of faith.
2
Identify the evidence
Look for the evidence Al-Ghazali provides: how did the early Muslims practice their faith? What did they study or not study? This supports his argument.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider Al-Ghazali's conclusion: why is it dangerous to judge someone as permanently in Hell if they only have simple faith? What does this tell us about Islamic theology?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم الإسلام ، والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، قد رفع القتال والقتل عنهم ، فأوجب حكم الإيمان والإسلام لمن قال : لا إله إلا الله ، وعقد عليها ؛ وهذه الكلمة لا تقتضي أكثر من إعتقاد الوجود والوحدة في الظاهر وعلى البديهة من غير نظر ؛ ثم سمعنا عمن قالها في صدر الإسلام ولم يعلم بعدها إلا فرائض الوضوء والصلاة ، الأعمال البدنية ، والكف عن أذى المسلم ؛ ولم يبلغنا أنهم تدارسوا علم الصفات وأحوالها ، ولأهل الله عالم بعلم ، أو عالم بنفسه ، أو هو باق ببقاء ، أو بنفسه ، وأشباه هذه المعارف ولا يدفع ظهور هذا إلا معاند أو جاهل بسيرة السلف ، وما جرى بينهم ، ويدل على قوة هذا الجانب في الشرع أن من استكشف منه على هذه الحالة وتحققت منه وأبى أن يذعن إلى تعلم ما زاد على ما عنده ، لم يفت أحد بقتله ولا باسترقاقه ، والحكم عليه بالخلود في النار ، عسير جداً وخطر عظيم ، مع ثبوت الشرع، بأن من قال : « لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة » اهـ
The judgment of Islam, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) lifted fighting and killing from them, so he made the judgment of faith (īmān) and submission (islām) obligatory for whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' and contracts upon it; and this word does not require more than the belief in existence and oneness outwardly and intuitively without reflection. Then we have heard from those who said it in the early period of Islam and knew after it only the obligations of ablution and prayer, bodily acts, and refraining from harming Muslims; and it has not reached us that they studied the science of attributes (ṣifāt) and their states, nor 'the knowledgeable of Allah is knowledgeable' or 'knower by essence' or 'He is eternal by eternity' or 'by essence' and similar such gnostic matters. And none denies the obviousness of this except an obstinate or ignorant of the conduct of the Salaf and what transpired among them. And it indicates the strength of this aspect in the Sharia that whoever is examined in this state and verified from him and refuses to submit to learning what is beyond what he has, no one has ruled to kill him or enslave him, and to judge him as permanently in the Fire is very difficult and a great danger, with the established Sharia that whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' enters Paradise.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the sufficiency of the simple declaration of faith. Al-Ghazali begins by stating that the ruling of Islam is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered the declaration of 'Lā ilāha illā Allāh' as sufficient to grant immunity from fighting and killing, thus making one a believer and Muslim. This word requires only a basic belief in God's existence and oneness, obtained intuitively without deep reflection. He then provides evidence from the early Muslims (ṣadr al-Islām) who knew only the basic obligations like wuḍū', prayer, and avoiding harm to Muslims, and did not engage in discussions of divine attributes (ṣifāt) or sophisticated theological terms like 'knowledge of Allah by knowledge' or 'eternal by eternity'. Al-Ghazali asserts that only an obstinate person or one ignorant of the Salaf's way would deny this. He concludes that it is extremely dangerous and difficult to judge such a person as permanently in Hell, because the Sharia establishes that whoever says 'Lā ilāha illā Allāh' enters Paradise.

السلف (Salaf)
علم الصفات (ʿilm al-ṣifāt)
إيمان (īmān)
إسلام (islām)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must understand and affirm detailed theological attributes to be saved.
Correction: Al-Ghazali argues that the simple declaration of faith, with basic belief in existence and oneness, is sufficient; early Muslims did not study such details.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali, what did the Prophet (peace be upon him) require for the judgment of faith and Islam?
A) Detailed knowledge of divine attributes
B) The declaration of 'Lā ilāha illā Allāh' along with basic belief
C) Intense study of kalam
D) Rejecting the world

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali argues that the simple declaration of faith suffices for salvation, and judging otherwise is a grave danger.

Al-Ghazali warns that judging another Muslim as destined for Hell is a 'great danger'. Have you ever harbored thoughts of condemnation towards someone whose practice or understanding seemed lacking? What step will you take this week to replace that judgment with mercy?

Ranks of the Siddiqeen and Muqarraboon in Tawhid
Ghazali describes the ranks of the siddiqeen and muqarraboon in tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchical spiritual ranks in tawhid, particularly the fourth rank (siddiqeen) and third rank (muqarraboon), and the distinction between muridun and muradun.

Core Idea
The siddiqeen see Allah first, then all things in relation to Him.

Ghazali explains that the disclosure of the secret of tawhid has degrees based on spiritual effort and purity. He distinguishes between those who see Allah directly (siddiqeen) and those who approach through a lower rank (muqarraboon). This passage also highlights the special status of the muradun and the spiritual hierarchy of qutb, awtad, and abdāl.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the contrast between degrees of disclosure and the analogy to sciences.
2
Identify the ranks
Find descriptions of the siddiqeen (fourth rank) and muqarraboon (third rank). Note how they perceive reality.
The siddiqeen see Allah first, then things as not other than Him.
3
Compare muridun and muradun
Contrast the seekers (muridun) who must pass through the third rank, and the desired ones (muradun) who begin at the fourth.
This shows two paths to the highest realization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانكشاف ذلك السر (۱) ، بل تلك الأسرار له درجات بحسب درجات وفي المجاهدة ودرجات الباطن ، في النظافة والطهارة عما سوى الله تعالى الإستضاءة بنور اليقين (۲) ، وذلك كتفاوت الخلق في أسرار الطب والفقه وسائر العلوم ، إذ يختلف ذلك بإختلاف الإجتهاد ، وإختلاف الفطرة، في الذكاء (٤) تلك الدرجات فكذلك هذه (ه) والفطنة (٣) ، وكما لا تنحصر (۳) لائحة ، وعاينوا حالات الإفتقار إلى الله عز وجل واضحة ، وسمعوا جميعها تدل على التوحيد راشدة ناصحة ، ثم رأوا الله عز وجل بإيمان قلوبهم ، وشاهدوه بغيب أرواحهم ، ولاحظوا جلاله وجماله بخفى أسرارهم ؛ وهم مع ذلك في درجات القرب على قدر حظ كل واحد منهم في اليقين ، وصفاء القلب . وأما الصديقون : فهم أهل المرتبة الرابعة في التوحيد ، وهؤلاء رأوا الله عز وجل، ثم رأوا الأشياء بعد ذلك فلم يروا في الدارين غيره ، ولا أطلعوا في الوجود على سواه ؛ والمريدون في الغالب لا بد لهم أن يحلو في المرتبة الثالثة ، وهي توحيد المقربين ، ومنها ينتقلون وعليها يعبرون إلى المرتبة الرابعة . وأما المرادون: فهم في الغالب مبتدئون بمقامهم الأخير، وهي المرتبة الرابعة ، ومتمسكنون فيها ، ومن أهل هذا المقام يكون القطب ، والأوتاد ، والبدلاء ، ومن أهل المرتبة الثالثة ، يكون النقباء والنجباء والشهداء والصالحون
And the disclosure of that secret (1), rather those secrets have degrees according to the degrees of mujahada and the degrees of the inner self, in purity and cleanliness from other than Allah, the illumination with the light of certainty (2), and that is like the disparity of creatures in the secrets of medicine, jurisprudence, and all sciences, for that differs according to the difference in ijtihad and the difference in innate disposition, in intelligence (4), so those degrees likewise this (5) and acumen (3), and as they are not limited (3) to a list, and they witnessed states of neediness towards Allah Almighty clearly, and they heard all of them indicating tawhid, rightly guiding, sincerely advising, then they saw Allah Almighty with the faith of their hearts, and they witnessed Him with the unseen of their souls, and they observed His majesty and beauty with the hidden of their secrets; and they are with that in degrees of nearness according to the share of each one of them in certainty and purity of heart. As for the siddiqeen: they are the people of the fourth rank in tawhid, and they saw Allah Almighty, then they saw things after that, so they did not see in the two abodes other than Him, nor did they perceive in existence other than Him. The muridun (seekers) for the most part must descend to the third rank, which is the tawhid of the muqarraboon (the near ones), and from it they transition and upon it they cross to the fourth rank. As for the muradun (the desired ones): they for the most part begin at their final station, which is the fourth rank, and they remain in it, and from the people of this station are the qutb, the awtad, and the abdāl; and from the people of the third rank are the nuqabā', the nujabā', the shuhadā', and the righteous.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the spiritual ranks of tawhid, specifically the fourth rank (siddiqeen) and the third rank (muqarraboon). The author begins by noting that the disclosure of the secret (the vision of Allah alone) has degrees based on mujahada and inner purification, just as knowledge in various sciences differs by effort and innate intelligence. He then describes how some people witness states of neediness towards Allah and see that all things point to tawhid. The siddiqeen (the truthful ones) are the people of the fourth rank: they see Allah first, and then they see things only in relation to Him, not seeing any existence besides Him. The muridun (seekers) typically must pass through the third rank (tawhid of the muqarraboon) before reaching the fourth. The muradun (the desired ones) usually begin at the fourth rank, which is their ultimate station. From this station come the spiritual leaders (qutb, awtad, abdāl), while from the third rank come the nuqabā', nujabā', shuhadā', and righteous. The passage emphasizes the superiority of direct divine vision and the hierarchical nature of spiritual realization.

Correction: The text clarifies that they see things after seeing Allah, but they do not see them as independent existences; they see all as manifestations of Allah.

Key Takeaway
The siddiqeen attain the highest rank by seeing Allah first and perceiving all things as signs of Him, not as independent realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the world around you—your job, your family, your daily tasks—do you see them as independent realities that distract you from Allah, or do you see them as signs that draw you closer to Him? What would need to change in your heart for you to be counted among the siddiqeen who see nothing except Him? This week, set aside five minutes each day to deliberately remind yourself that everything exists by and for Allah.
?
The passage says the muridun must descend to the third rank before reaching the fourth. Are you willing to embrace spiritual struggle (mujahada) and inner purification, even if it means temporarily stepping back from worldly comforts? What specific struggle have you been avoiding because it feels too difficult? Commit to one small act of purification today.
?
The muradun begin at the highest rank—not by their own effort but by divine grace. Do you rely more on your own striving or on Allah's gift? How can you cultivate a balance between sincere effort (as a murid) and humble reliance on being chosen (as a murad)? Reflect on a time when you felt Allah's grace overtook your efforts, and thank Him for it.

The Debate on Claiming Iman and Paradise
Imam Ghazali narrates a debate between Ibn Mas'ud and Yazid on claiming iman and paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between faith (iman) and certainty of entering Paradise, and why early Muslims distinguished between declaring oneself a believer and claiming Paradise.

Core Idea
Faith does not guarantee Paradise; sin leaves hope and fear.

This lesson presents a historical debate between the companion Ibn Mas'ud and Yazid ibn 'Amirah. Ibn Mas'ud initially thought that claiming to be a believer is equivalent to claiming Paradise. Yazid corrects him, explaining that faith includes beliefs and actions, but sins remain a factor. This story illustrates the humble attitude of the early Muslims regarding their standing with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the exchange: Ibn Mas'ud's claim, Yazid's response, and Ibn Mas'ud's final admission.
Pay attention to the key term 'zalla' (slip) – it shows that even a companion could make a theological error.
2
Identify the two positions
What does Ibn Mas'ud assert? That saying 'I am a believer' is like saying 'I am in Paradise.' What is Yazid's correction? He defines iman as belief in six articles and performance of acts, and notes that sins prevent certainty of forgiveness, so one cannot claim Paradise.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Why did Ibn Mas'ud accept the correction? What does this teach about the proper attitude toward faith? Consider how this applies to your own understanding of iman and hope for Paradise.
This story emphasizes humility and reliance on Allah's mercy.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وناظر عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه يزيد بن عميرة في الإيمان ، فقال عبد الله : لو قلت إني مؤمن لقلت إني في الجنة ، فقال له يزيد بن عميرة : يا صاحب رسول الله هذه زلة منك ، وهل الإيمان إلا أن تؤمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله والبعث والميزان وتقيم الصلاة والصوم والزكاة ، ولنا ذنوب لو نعلم أنها تغفر لنا لعلمنا أننا من أهل الجنة ، فمن أجل ذلك نقول إنا مؤمنون ولا نقول إنا من أهل الجنة ، فقال ابن مسعود : صدقت والله إنها مني زلة
And 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) debated Yazid ibn 'Amirah about faith (al-iman). 'Abdullah said: 'If I said I am a believer, I would say I am in Paradise.' Yazid ibn 'Amirah said to him: 'O companion of the Messenger of Allah, this is a slip from you. Is faith (al-iman) anything but that you believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the resurrection, the scale, and you establish prayer, fasting, and zakat? We have sins; if we knew they were forgiven, we would know we are among the people of Paradise. For that reason we say we are believers, but we do not say we are among the people of Paradise.' Ibn Mas'ud said: 'You have spoken the truth; by Allah, it was a slip from me.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage narrates a historical debate between the prominent companion 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Yazid ibn 'Amirah about the implications of declaring oneself a believer (mu'min). Ibn Mas'ud initially asserts that saying 'I am a believer' is tantamount to claiming Paradise, highlighting the gravity of such a statement. Yazid corrects him, explaining that faith (iman) is defined by belief in Allah, angels, books, messengers, resurrection, and the scale, and by performing acts of worship like prayer, fasting, and zakat. He argues that they have sins, and without knowing whether those sins are forgiven, they cannot claim to be certain of Paradise. Therefore, they say 'We are believers' without claiming Paradise. Ibn Mas'ud concedes, admitting his slip. The passage illustrates the early Muslim understanding that iman does not guarantee Paradise due to unatoned sins, and that one should not arrogantly claim a status not assured by divine forgiveness.

Key Terms
الإيمان
المؤمن
الجنة
الزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Claiming to be a believer (mu'min) automatically means certainty of entering Paradise.
Correction: As Yazid explains, iman includes belief and actions, but sins prevent knowledge of forgiveness, so one cannot claim Paradise. The correct stance is to say 'I am a believer' while leaving Paradise to Allah's mercy.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Yazid ibn 'Amirah say that believers should not claim they are from the people of Paradise?
A) Because iman is only belief in six articles and does not include actions.
B) Because they have sins and do not know if those sins are forgiven.
C) Because Paradise is only for prophets.
D) Because Ibn Mas'ud had committed a major sin.

Key Takeaway
Early Muslims distinguished between being a believer (mu'min) and being guaranteed Paradise, because sins remained a factor of uncertainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to say 'I am a believer' right now, would your heart also whisper to you 'and I am guaranteed Paradise'? What does that whisper reveal about your reliance on your own deeds versus Allah's mercy?
?
Reflect on a sin you committed recently. Did you truly feel uncertain about your standing with Allah because of it, or did you assume it was minor and automatically forgiven? How does this lesson challenge that assumption?
?
Ibn Mas'ud immediately admitted his slip. When was the last time you were able to admit a theological error in your own thinking about faith? What holds you back from that humility?

Protection from Deviation and the Method of Combining Reason and Revelation
Commentator defines zaygh and ilhad and outlines the Sunni methodology for combining reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah protects the people of Sunnah from deviation and heresy, and how they combine rational inquiry with transmitted revelation.

Core Idea
The straight path combines reason with revelation, guided by the Qur'an and the Salaf.

This lesson unpacks the commentator's explanation of how the people of Sunnah are safeguarded from two dangerous deviations: zaygh (straying) and ilhad (heresy). The passage defines these terms and presents a methodology that holds reason and revelation in harmony, refuting those who distort texts or abandon them.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage and translation
Start by reading the entire Arabic passage with its literal translation. Notice how the main sentence is followed by four explanatory footnotes that clarify key terms.
This passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the definitions of zaygh and ilhad
Footnote (1) defines zaygh as deviation from truth and ilhad as straying into error. Note the two types of ilhad: shirk with Allah and shirk with causes, and the two forms of ilhad in Allah's names.
Understand that the first type of ilhad destroys faith; the second only weakens it.
3
Grasp the methodology: strong rope and clear path
Footnotes (2) and (3) explain the 'strong rope' as the Qur'an and the 'clear path' as following the Salaf. See how this refutes those who manipulate texts with reason alone.
The commentator hints at refuting Mu'tazila and philosophers.
4
Understand the combination of reason and transmitted reports
Footnote (4) clarifies that transmitted rulings from revelation are combined with rational investigation. This elevates the status of theoretical inquiry when done in accordance with the Book and Sunna.
This is the ultimate outcome: accepting both intellect and transmitted knowledge.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضلال الملحدين (۱) ، ووفقهم للإقتداء بسيد المرسلين ، وسددهم للتأسي بصحبه الأكرمين ، ويسر لهم إقتفاء آثار السلف الصالحين حتى اعتصموا من مقتضيات العقول بالحبل المتين(۲) ، ومن سير الأولين وعقائدهم بالمنهج (۳) المبين ، فجمعوا بالقبول بين نتائج العقول وقضايا الشرع المنقول (٤)
(۱) الزيغ الميل عن الإستقامة والخروج عن نهج الحق ، والمراد بالزائغين : هم أهل البدع القبيحة الذين أحد توافى العقائد بمجرد التشهي ما يؤدي إلى تشبية أو تعطيل
والمراد بضلال الملحدين : غوايتهم ، والملحد المائل عن الحق ، والإلحاد ضربان : إلحاد إلى الشرك بالله ، وإلحاد إلى الشرك بالأسباب ، فالأول ينافي الإيمان ويبطله ، والثاني يوهي عراه ولا يبطله ، والإلحاد في أسمائه تعالى على وجيهن : أحدهما أن يوصف بما لا يصح وصفه به والثاني أن تتأول أوصافه على ما لا يليق به
(۲) القوي الذي لا ينقطع بمن تعلق به واستمسك ، وبهذا المعنى جاءت صفة القرآن في الحديث ، وفيه تلميح الرد على المعتزلة والفلاسفة فإنهم تصرفوا في الألفاظ بمقتضى عقولهم ، فأولوا وبدلوا .
(۳) وفي بعض النسخ بالنهج وهو الطريق الواضح المسلوك ، والمعنى سيروا في سير الأولين ونحلهم التي انتحلوها ، فما وافق الكتاب والسنة وآثار السلف أخذوا به ، وما خالف تركوه
(٤) يعني القضايا التي قضى بها الشرع ، ونقل لنا ذلك الثقات ، والقضية قول يصح أن يقال لقائله صادق أو كاذب فيه ، وفيه تلميح إلى رفع شأن أهل النظر والبحث في العقائد على مقتضى الكتاب والسنة حيث جمعوا بين العقل والنقل
And the misguidance of the atheists (1), and He guided them to follow the master of the messengers, and set them right to emulate his most noble companions, and facilitated for them to follow the traces of the righteous predecessors until they clung from the dictates of the intellect to the strong rope (2), and from the conduct of the predecessors and their beliefs to the clear path (3), so they accepted and combined the results of the intellects and the transmitted rulings of the law (4). (1) Al-zaygh is deviation from uprightness and departure from the path of truth. What is meant by al-za'ighun are the people of evil innovations who adopt beliefs based on mere desire, leading to tashbih or ta'til. What is meant by 'the misguidance of the atheists' is their error. Al-ilhad is deviation from the truth. Al-ilhad is of two types: ilhad to shirk with Allah, and ilhad to shirk with causes. The first negates faith and invalidates it, the second weakens its ties but does not invalidate it. Ilhad in His names, Exalted is He, is in two ways: one is describing Him with what is not appropriate for Him, and the second is interpreting His attributes in a way that is not befitting. (2) The strong rope that does not break for those who cling to it. In this sense, the attribute of the Qur'an came in the hadith. In it is a hint of refutation against the Mu'tazila and the philosophers, for they manipulated the texts according to their intellects, so they interpreted and altered. (3) In some copies, 'al-nahj' which is the clear path. The meaning: they followed the conduct of the predecessors and the doctrines they adopted; whatever agreed with the Book, the Sunna, and the effects of the Salaf, they accepted; whatever opposed, they left. (4) Meaning the rulings that the law has judged, and those were transmitted to us by reliable authorities. Al-qadiyya is a statement about which it is valid to say to its speaker 'true' or 'false.' In it is a hint to elevating the status of the people of theoretical investigation in beliefs according to the Book and the Sunna, as they combined reason and transmitted reports.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage explains how Allah protected the people of Sunna from deviation and guided them to follow the Prophet and Salaf, and how they integrated reason and revelation. The footnote (1) defines 'zaygh' (deviation) as straying from the path of truth, and 'ilhad' (atheism/heresy) as deviation from truth, detailing two types: ilhad toward shirk with Allah and ilhad toward shirk with causes. The first destroys faith, the second weakens it. It also describes ilhad in Allah's names. Footnote (2) defines the 'strong rope' as the Qur'an, and refutes the Mu'tazila and philosophers who distorted texts with reason. Footnote (3) clarifies the methodology of following the Salaf: accepting what agrees with the Book, Sunna, and Salaf, and leaving what contradicts. Footnote (4) explains that 'transmitted rulings' are those from revelation, and this passage elevates the status of rational investigation in creed when combined with transmitted texts.

إلحاد
تشبيه
تعطيل
الحبل المتين
المنهج
قضايا الشرع المنقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All ilhad is the same and completely invalidates faith.
Correction: The commentator distinguishes between ilhad toward shirk with Allah (which negates faith) and ilhad toward shirk with causes (which only weakens faith but does not invalidate it).

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the difference between the two types of ilhad?
A) The first is in beliefs, the second in actions.
B) The first negates faith and invalidates it; the second weakens its ties but does not invalidate it.

D) The first is committed by philosophers, the second by Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni approach avoids both zaygh and ilhad by adhering to the Qur'an and the Salaf, and by harmonizing reason with revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
You claim to follow the Qur'an and Sunna, but do you truly accept the results of rational investigation only when they agree with the transmitted texts? Examine a recent situation where you prioritized your own reasoning over revelation—what will you do differently now?

The Fourth Chapter: An Introduction to Faith and Islam
Ghazali introduces the fourth chapter with a summary of topics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of Ghazali's fourth chapter: its topics of faith, Islam, their relationship, increase/decrease, and the Salaf's exception.

Core Idea
Faith and Islam are related but distinct — this chapter unpacks their connection.

Before diving into the detailed discussions of faith and Islam, Ghazali provides a chapter overview. This passage outlines the major themes: the connection and separation between iman and islam, whether faith increases or decreases, and why early Muslims sometimes said 'if Allah wills' about their faith. This lesson sets the stage for the three issues that follow.

The passage lists four areas: (1) faith and Islam, (2) their connection and separation, (3) increase and decrease, (4) the aspect of the Salaf's exception. Find each in the text.
These topics will be explored in detail in the chapter's three issues.

The introduction serves as a roadmap for the chapter.
